Preference of Nominal Sentences in Divine Praise: A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Explaining why the author chose 'alhamdu lillah' instead of 'ahmadu lillah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three reasons Hanafi usul prefers the nominal sentence 'alhamdu lillah' over the verbal 'ahmadu lillah' for praising Allah, and apply the usul principle that nominal sentences indicate permanence (thubut) while verbal sentences indicate temporality (huduth).

Core Idea
Nominal sentences affirm Allah's eternal worthiness of praise; verbal sentences risk implying praise is initiated by the creature.

In this passage from 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut', the commentator explains why the author began with 'alhamdu lillah' rather than a verbal phrase. The discussion reveals a key Hanafi usul principle: linguistic form must match the nature of the object of praise. Since Allah is eternally praiseworthy, the nominal form is more appropriate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sentence types
Recognize that 'alhamdu lillah' is a nominal sentence (jumla ismiyya) starting with a noun, while 'ahmadu lillah' is a verbal sentence (jumla fi'liyya) starting with a verb. The distinction is central to the argument.
In Arabic grammar, nominal sentences denote stability and continuity; verbal sentences denote events or actions that occur in time.
2
Analyze the Quranic precedent
The commentator’s first reason: The Qur'an itself begins with the nominal 'alhamdu lillah' (Surah al-Fatiha, 1:2). This sets the highest precedent for choosing the nominal form when praising Allah.
This reason is one of tawqif (following divine guidance) rather than pure linguistic reasoning.
3
Understand the linguistic indication (dalala)
The second reason: The verbal 'ahmadu lillah' indicates temporality (huduth) – that the act of praising originates from the speaker. The nominal 'alhamdu lillah' indicates permanence (thubut wa dawam) – that Allah is inherently worthy of praise, independent of any creature’s action. Thus, the nominal form is more accurate.
This reason is rooted in Hanafi usul: the form of the sentence affects the meaning (dalala) and must align with the attribute being described.
4
Consider the sincerity condition (qalb)
The third reason: Praise (hamd) is a quality of the heart. Uttering 'ahmadu lillah' is a report that one is actively praising, which becomes false if the heart is heedless. 'Alhamdu lillah' does not entail such a report; it is a statement of fact about Allah’s worthiness, not necessarily about the speaker's current state. Hence it is safer and more sincere.
This shows the Hanafi concern for avoiding falsehood in acts of worship and the importance of congruence between speech and inner state.
5
Apply the usul principle
From these reasons, derive the general Hanafi rule: When describing Allah’s eternal attributes, prefer nominal constructions because they convey stability (thubut) and avoid implying temporality or change in Allah. This principle extends to other contexts like praise and glorification.
This is a usul rule that governs word choice in theological and ritual contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوال:۔ مقام محمد میں مصنف نے جملہ اسمیہ الحمد للہ کہا، احمداللہ یامحمدہ وغیرہ کیوں نہیں کہا۔ جواب : کئی وجوہ سے مقام حمد میں جملہ اسمیہ کو فعلیہ پر ترجیح حاصل ہے۔ اس لئے اسمیہ کو اختیار کیا۔
(الف) سب سے افضل و مقدس از لی کتاب قرآن حکیم کی ابتداء الحمد للہ جملہ اسمیہ سے ہے۔ (ب) احمد اللہ فعلیہ ہے جو حدوث پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور الحمد للہ اسمیہ ہے جو ثبوت و دوام پر دلالت کرتا ہے پس اس مقام میں جملہ فعلیہ لانے سے یہ ضعیف احتمال پایا جاتا ہے کہ بندہ حامد اللہ کی حمد کرنے پر قادر ہے اور اس کے حمد کرنے سے ہی حدوث حمد ہوا ہے اس کے برخلاف اسمیہ میں صراحتاً دلالت اس پر ہوتی ہے کہ اللہ عز شانہ حمد حامدین اور شکر شاکرین سے پیشتر ہی از لا وابدا محمود ہے خواہ کوئی اس کی حمد بیان کرے خواہ نہ بیان کرے چنانچہ قرآن حکیم میں بھی اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اللہ عز شانہ کے لئے حمد ذاتی ثابت ہے کہ وہ عالمین کا رب ہے غرض استحقاق حمد ذاتا اللہ تعالی کا حق ہے اور یہ ظاہر کہ جو لفظ لذاتہ استحقاق حمد پر صر ا حنا دلالت کرے وہ بہر حال اولی دار حج ہے اس لفظ ۔ ۔ جس میں یشبہ پایا جائے کر شخص واحد کی حمد سے حدوث حمد پایا گیا۔
(ج) حمد صفت قلب سے عبارت ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ بوقت حمد حامد اسبات کا اعتقاد صحیح رکھے کہ محمود حقیقی مفصلا منعم حقیقی ہونے کے سبب مسحق تعظیم ہے پس اس تقدیر پر کہ حمد صفت قلبی ہے اگر کسی انسان نے احمد اللہ کا تلفظ کیا اس حال میں کہ اس کا قلب معنی تعظیم سے غافل ہے تو یقیناً اس وقت اس قائل کا احمد اللہ کہنا لا بلکہ کاذب ہوگا کیونکہ انہوں نے زبانی طور پر حامد ہونے کی خبر دی ہے جبکہ وہ قلبی طور پر حامد نہیں ہے کہ اس کا قلب ربط احمد سے عاری و غافل ہے۔ اس کے برعکس کسی بندہ نے اگر الحمد للہ کا
Question: In the context of praise, the author used the nominal sentence 'alhamdu lillah', why did he not say 'ahmadu lillah' or 'ya muhammadah' etc.? Answer: For several reasons, the nominal sentence is preferred over the verbal sentence in the context of praise. Therefore, the nominal was chosen. (A) The beginning of the most virtuous and sacred book, the Noble Qur'an, starts with the nominal sentence 'alhamdu lillah'. (B) 'Ahmadu lillah' is verbal, indicating temporality, while 'alhamdu lillah' is nominal, indicating permanence and continuity. So using the verbal sentence in this context carries the weak possibility that the servant is able to praise Allah, and praise is initiated by his action. In contrast, the nominal sentence explicitly indicates that Allah, exalted is His glory, is worthy of praise before any praise of praisers, eternally, whether anyone praises Him or not. Accordingly, the Qur'an points to this: that Allah has essential praise, as He is the Lord of the worlds. In short, deserving praise is essentially Allah's right, and it is clear that a word which explicitly indicates deserving praise is superior to a word in which there is a semblance that praise is originated from a single person. (C) Praise is a quality of the heart, meaning that at the time of praise, the praiser should hold the correct belief that the real praised one, due to being the true benefactor, deserves glorification. So on the basis that praise is a heart quality, if a person utters 'ahmadu lillah' while his heart is heedless of the meaning of glorification, then indeed his statement 'ahmadu lillah' is false because he has verbally reported being a praiser while he is not a praiser in heart, his heart being devoid of the connection of 'ahmada. Conversely, if a servant says 'alhamdu lillah'...
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of why the author of the matn chose the nominal sentence 'alhamdu lillah' over a verbal form like 'ahmadu lillah' for the context of praise. Three reasons are given from a Hanafi usul perspective. First, the Quran itself begins with the nominal 'alhamdu lillah', establishing the precedent. Second, the nominal form indicates stability and continuity (thubut wa dawam), while the verbal form implies temporality and occurrence (huduth). Using the verbal could imply that the act of praise is initiated by the servant, whereas the nominal emphasizes that Allah is inherently worthy of praise, independent of creation. Third, praise is a quality of the heart (sifat qalb); the nominal form does not require the speaker to be in a state of praise, whereas the verbal 'ahmadu lillah' is a report of the speaker's own praise, which would be false if the heart is heedless. Thus, the nominal form is safer and more appropriate for glorifying Allah.

Key Terms
جملہ اسمیہ (jumla ismiyya): A nominal sentence that begins with a noun, indicating permanence and stability.
جملہ فعلیہ (jumla fi'liyya): A verbal sentence that begins with a verb, indicating temporality and occurrence.
حدوث (huduth): Temporality or origination in time, as opposed to eternity.
ثبوت (thubut): Permanence, stability, and continuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a reason the nominal sentence 'alhamdu lillah' is preferred over the verbal 'ahmadu lillah'?
A) It is the shortest form.
B) It indicates that Allah is eternally praiseworthy, independent of anyone's praise.
C) It was revealed to Prophet Muhammad in a dream.
D) It avoids the need for sincerity in the heart.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, nominal sentences are preferred for divine praise because they convey Allah's eternal worthiness (thubut) and avoid implying temporality (huduth) from the creature's action.

The Linguistic Nature of 'Allah': Proper Noun or Description?
Usul analysis of the linguistic status of 'Allah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main positions on the linguistic nature of 'Allah' and evaluate the proofs for each using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Whether 'Allah' is a proper noun or a description impacts the meaning of tawhid and Quranic interpretation.

The word 'Allah' is the most sacred term in Islam, yet its linguistic classification has been debated by scholars. This lesson examines the two views: that it is a proper noun (علم) or a derived description (وصف). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping Hanafi usul and the theological concept of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions and their proponents
From the passage, note the majority view (proper noun) held by verifiers like Khalil, Sibawayh, and most usuliyyun/fuqaha, and the minority view (description) held by 'some scholars'.
The majority view is explicitly called the 'chosen view' (مذهب مختار).
2
Analyze the proofs for the proper noun view
Examine the two proofs: (1) if derived, 'la ilaha illallah' would not be pure tawhid; (2) 'Allah' always appears as a described noun, never as a description.
These proofs rely on usul principles about proper nouns and exclusive indication.
3
Analyze the proofs for the description view
Examine the three proofs: (a) the Essence is inconceivable, so no word can indicate it directly; (b) verse 'Allah is light' would be problematic if proper noun; (c) etymological relationship with roots.
The description view argues that 'Allah' became exclusive through prevalent usage (غلبہ).
4
Understand the theological implications
Note that if 'Allah' is a proper noun, tawhid is absolute and exclusive; if a description, there is some conceptual sharing. This affects interpretation of Quranic verses.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical difference in meaning.
5
Determine the preferred view in Hanafi usul
The text clearly prefers the proper noun view, aligning with the majority and verifiers. This is the mufta bihi position for Hanafis.
The Hanafi school follows this view to safeguard pure tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ ۔ اللہ نظم اللہ اسم جلالت کے تعلق سے محققین کا مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ یہ غفظ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا اسم علم ہے غیر مشتق ہے یہی روایت خلیل وسیبویہ سے بھی منقول ہے اور اکثر اصولیین وفقہاء کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ علمیت کی بنیا د دو باتوں پر ہے۔ (۱) ایک یہ کہ اگر علم نہ ہو مشتق ہو تو اس لفظ کی دلالت معنی کلی پر ہوگی ذات پر نہیں ہوسکتی کیونکہ مفہوم وضعی کثیرین کے درمیان شرکت سے مانع نہیں ہوتا ، پس کلمہ لا الہ الا اللہ لا الہ الا الرحمن کی طرح توحید حقیقی نہیں رہ جائے گا جبکہ تمام عقلاء کا اجماع ہے کہ لا الہ الا الله توحید محض ہے بر عکس "لاالہ الا الرحمن کے لیکن جب لفظ اللہ کو ذات واحدہ معینہ متجمعہ جمیع صفات کمالیہ کا علم قرار دیا جائے تو توحید محض ہو نا بغیر کسی شبہ کے یقینی ہو جاتا ہے۔ (۲) دوسرے یہ کہ لفظ اللہ دوسرے اسماء البیہ کا ہمیشہ موصوف بنکر ہی مستعمل ہوتا ہے کبھی وصف بنگر استعمال نہیں ہوتا۔ قرآن کریم میں ہے اللہ الواحد القہار، اس کے علاوہ دوسرے اسماء مبارکہ جب کبھی مستعمل ہوتے ہیں تو وہ اسماء وصف ہی بنگر مستعمل ہوتے ہیں لہذا اسم ہو نا زیادہ ظاہر ، چونکہ یہ اسم ذات الہی کے ساتھ مختص ہے غیر پر اس کا اطلاق قطعار و انہیں اس لئے یہ لفظ اسی ذات کا علم ہو گیا۔ بعض علماء اس طرف گئے ہیں کہ یہ لفظ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا علم نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ لفظ اصل کے اعتبار سے وصف ہے لیکن یہ ایسا وصف ہے جو صرف ذات باری ہی کے لئے بطور غلبہ مستعمل ہے غیر کے لئے اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہو سکتا ، حاصل یہ کہ یہ ایسا وصف ہے جو علم کی طرح خاص ہو گیا ۔ ہے جیسے شریا وصعق کہ حقیقت میں یہ دونوں وصف ہی ہیں مگر غلبہ استعمال کی وجہ سے بمنزلہ علم ہوگئے ہیں اس لئے جس طرح علم خود وصف نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اوصاف اس پر محمول ہوتے ہیں اور علم میں غیر کی شرکت بھی نہیں ہوتی اسی طرح اس میں غیر کی شرکت نہ ہوگی مگر اور علم کی طرح اس پر اوصاف محمول و متصف ہو نگے ۔ وصف ہونے کی ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذات باری تعالی من حیث ذات قطع نظر صفات حقیقیہ اضافیہ کے، غیر مدرک بالکنہ بلکہ بشر کے لئے غیر معقول ہے یعنی بشر کی قوت مدرکہ میں متصور نہیں ہوسکتی اور جب اس کی ذات غیر معقول تو کوئی لفظ بھی اس کی ذات پر دال نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ الفاظ معنی پہنی پر دلالت کرتے ہیں اور ذات من حیث الذات ادراک عقل اور حصول فی الاذھان سے ماوراء ہوتی ہے اب اگر کوئی لفظ اس کی ذات مخصوصہ پر دلالت کرنے کے لئے موضوع ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس لفظ کی دلالت اس کی ذات پر ممکن ہوگی حالانکہ کسی بھی لفظ کی دلالت اس کی ذات پر باطل کہ لفظ کی دلالت علی مافی الاذھان ہوتی ہے اور لفظ اللہ کا مصداق ماوراء اذھان وعقول ہے لہذا وہ جو مافی الاذھان پر دلالت کرتا ہے وہ ماوراء اذھان پر کیونکر دال ہوسکتا ہے؟ وصفیت کی دوسری وجہ : لفظ اللہ وصف نہ ہو علم ہو تو اللہ عز شانہ کا ارشاد۔ اللہ نور السموات والارض کا معنی بغیر کسی تاویل کے صحیح نہ ہوگا بلکہ باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بر تقدیر علمیت آیت کا معنی ہوگا کہ ذات مشخص آسمان وزمین کا نور ہے جبکہ ذات وحدہ لاشریک کا آسمان میں ہونا بدلہبتہ باطل کہ وہ زمان ومکان سے منزہ اور مبرا ہے البتہ اگر وصف مانیں تو آیت متلوہ کے معنی میں کوئی فساد لازم نہیں آتا ہے اس لئے کہ اس تقدیر پر آیت کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ معبود آسمان وزمین کا نور ہے۔ وصفیت کی تیسری وجہ :۔ یہ ہے اس لفظ اور اسکے مبادی اشتقاق میں معنی اشتقاقی پایا جاتا ہے۔ معنی اشتقاقی موجود ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مشتق کا مشتق منہ کے لفظ اور معنی میں شریک ہونا ، چنانچہ لفظ اللہ کے جتنے ماخذ و مبادی تفسیر میں بیان کئے گئے ہیں ہر ایک مبدا کے ساتھ اس کو مناسبت نام حاصل ہے لہذا اس کا مشتق ہو نازیادہ ظاہر ہے وھو تعالی اعلم۔
His statement: 'Allah' – Regarding the word 'Allah', the chosen view of the verifiers is that it is a proper noun (ism 'alam) for the Essence of Allah, not derived (ghayr mushtaq). This narration is also transmitted from Khalil and Sibawayh, and most usuliyyun and fuqaha hold this view. The basis of its being a proper noun is two things: (1) If it were not a proper noun but derived, its indication would be upon a general meaning, not on the Essence, because a lexical concept does not prevent sharing among many. Thus, the phrase 'la ilaha illallah' would not be pure tawhid like 'la ilaha illa al-rahman', whereas all rational people agree that 'la ilaha illallah' is pure tawhid, contrary to 'la ilaha illa al-rahman'. But if the word 'Allah' is considered a proper noun for the unique Essence possessing all perfect attributes, then pure tawhid becomes certain without any doubt. (2) Secondly, the word 'Allah' is always used as the described (mawsuf), never as a description (sifah). In the Qur'an it is: 'Allah, the One, the Subduer'. Other blessed names are used as descriptions, so it being a noun is more apparent. Since it is specific to the Divine Essence, its application to others is impossible, thus it has become a proper noun for that Essence. Some scholars have inclined that this word is not a proper noun but is originally a description, but it is a description that is used exclusively for the Divine Essence by way of prevalence (ghalabah), not applicable to others. The conclusion is that it is a description that has become specific like a proper noun, like 'Sharya' and 'Sa'q' which are actually descriptions but due to prevalent usage have become like proper nouns. Therefore, just as a proper noun itself is not a description but descriptions are predicated upon it, and no other shares in it, similarly no other will share in it, and descriptions will be predicated upon it as with a proper noun. One reason for its being a description is that the Essence of Allah, in itself, without considering real and relational attributes, is not fully comprehended; rather it is inconceivable for humans. When His Essence is inconceivable, no word can indicate it, because words indicate mental meanings, and the Essence itself is beyond intellectual perception and mental acquisition. Now if a word is posited to indicate that specific Essence, its indication upon that Essence would be impossible, because a word indicates what is in the mind, and the object of 'Allah' is beyond minds and intellects. So how can that which indicates what is in the mind indicate what is beyond minds? A second reason for its being a description: If 'Allah' were a proper noun not a description, then Allah's saying: 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth' would not be correct without ta'wil; rather it would be invalid, because on the assumption of it being a proper noun, the meaning would be that the specific Essence is the light of the heavens and earth, whereas the unique Essence being in the heavens is obviously invalid, as He is transcendent beyond time and place. However, if we consider it a description, no corruption follows in the meaning of the recited verse, because on this assumption the meaning would be: 'The Deity is the light of the heavens and the earth.' A third reason for its being a description: There is an etymological meaning (ma'na ishtiqaqi) between this word and its derivational bases. The presence of an etymological meaning means that the derived word shares with its root in word and meaning. Thus, whatever origins and bases are mentioned in tafsir for the word 'Allah', it has an appropriate relationship with each basis. Therefore, it being derived is more apparent. And He, Most High, knows best.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic and theological analysis of the word 'Allah', a core topic in usul al-fiqh regarding the definition of a term. The commentator presents two main positions: 1) The majority view (including verifiers like Khalil and Sibawayh, and most usuliyyun and fuqaha, which includes the Hanafi school) that 'Allah' is a proper noun (علم) for the Divine Essence, not derived. They give two proofs: first, if derived, it would indicate a general meaning, undermining the unique tawhid of 'la ilaha illallah'; second, it always appears as a described noun, not as a description. 2) A minority view that it is originally a description (وصف) but has become exclusive through prevalent usage (غلبہ), like 'Sharya' and 'Sa'q'. The text then gives three arguments for the description view: (a) the Essence is inconceivable, so no word can indicate it directly; (b) the verse 'Allah is the light of the heavens and earth' would be problematic if 'Allah' is a proper noun implying physical location; (c) there is an etymological relationship with roots, indicating derivation. The commentary does not explicitly prefer one view but presents both, with the first being the 'chosen view' (مذهب مختار). The Hanafi position aligns with the majority that it is a proper noun, as it preserves the unicity of tawhid and avoids anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
الله (Allah): The name of the Divine Essence, either a proper noun (علم) or a description (وصف) that has become exclusive.
اسم علم (ism 'alam): A proper noun that indicates a specific entity without sharing with others.
وصف (wasf / sifah): A descriptive attribute that originally indicates a meaning shared with others.
غلبہ (ghalabah): Prevalent usage that makes a common word exclusive to a specific entity.
توحید محض (tawhid mahd): Pure monotheism that admits no partner in divinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars argue that 'Allah' is a description (وصف) rather than a proper noun?
A) Because it is used by both Muslims and non-Muslims.
B) Because the verse 'Allah is the light of the heavens and earth' would otherwise imply physical location.
C) Because it has no etymological root.
D) Because it is derived from a verb.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following the majority of verifiers, holds that 'Allah' is a proper noun (علم غير مشتق), ensuring the absolute uniqueness of God in tawhid.

Is 'Allah' a Description or a Proper Name? A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Linguistic-theological analysis of 'Allah' as sifah vs 'alam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi arguments for classifying 'Allah' as a sifah (description) and apply the principle that a word indicating an inconceivable essence must be a description.

Core Idea
The word 'Allah' is a description that became exclusive through predominant usage, not a proper name.

This passage tackles a foundational question in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: is the word 'Allah' a descriptive attribute (sifah) or a proper name ('alam)? The answer has implications for how we interpret Quranic verses and understand the divine names. The commentator presents three compelling arguments—epistemological, theological, and linguistic—that together establish 'Allah' as a description that functions like a proper name due to exclusive usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the debate is whether 'Allah' is a description (sifah) or a proper name ('alam). Notice the text concludes it is a description that has become like a proper name through predominant usage (ghalabah al-istimal).
The example of 'Shari' and 'Sa'q' illustrates words that are descriptions but act like proper names.
2
Analyze the first argument (epistemological)
The commentator argues that since Allah's essence is imperceptible and beyond mental representation, no word can directly denote His essence. Therefore, 'Allah' must denote an attribute (e.g., being worshipped) rather than the essence itself.
This relies on the Hanafi principle that words indicate meanings in the mind (mafahim dhihniyyah).
3
Analyze the second argument (theological)
If 'Allah' were a proper name, the verse 'Allahu nur al-samawati wa al-ard' would imply the specific essence is located in the heavens, leading to anthropomorphism. Taking it as a description (object of worship) avoids this corruption.
Consider how a proper name would make the verse problematic, while a description allows a non-literal interpretation.
4
Analyze the third argument (linguistic)
The word 'Allah' shares a derivational relationship with its roots (e.g., ilah). A proper name is typically primitive and not derived, so the presence of derivational meaning supports it being a description.
Derivational meaning means the word is mushtaq (derived) rather than jamid (solid).
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if 'Allah' is a description, it can be derived and attributes can be attached to it; if a proper name, it cannot be derived and would require anthropomorphic interpretation of verses.
This shows how usul analysis directly impacts fiqh and tafsir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت اعتبار سے وصف ہے لیکن یہ ایسا وصف ہے جو صرف ذات باری ہی کے لئے بطور غلبہ مستعمل ہے غیر کے لئے اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہو سکتا ، حاصل یہ کہ یہ ایسا وصف ہے جو علم کی طرح خاص ہو گیا ۔ ہے جیسے شریا وصعق کہ حقیقت میں یہ دونوں وصف ہی ہیں مگر غلبہ استعمال کی وجہ سے بمنزلہ علم ہوگئے ہیں اس لئے جس طرح علم خود وصف نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اوصاف اس پر محمول ہوتے ہیں اور علم میں غیر کی شرکت بھی نہیں ہوتی اسی طرح اس میں غیر کی شرکت نہ ہوگی مگر اور علم کی طرح اس پر اوصاف محمول و متصف ہو نگے ۔ وصف ہونے کی ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذات باری تعالی من حیث ذات قطع نظر صفات حقیقیہ اضافیہ کے، غیر مدرک بالکنہ بلکہ بشر کے لئے غیر معقول ہے یعنی بشر کی قوت مدرکہ میں متصور نہیں ہوسکتی اور جب اس کی ذات غیر معقول تو کوئی لفظ بھی اس کی ذات پر دال نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ الفاظ معنی پہنی پر دلالت کرتے ہیں اور ذات من حیث الذات ادراک عقل اور حصول فی الاذھان سے ماوراء ہوتی ہے اب اگر کوئی لفظ اس کی ذات مخصوصہ پر دلالت کرنے کے لئے موضوع ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ اس لفظ کی دلالت اس کی ذات پر ممکن ہوگی حالانکہ کسی بھی لفظ کی دلالت اس کی ذات پر باطل کہ لفظ کی دلالت علی مافی الاذھان ہوتی ہے اور لفظ اللہ کا مصداق ماوراء اذھان وعقول ہے لہذا وہ جو مافی الاذھان پر دلالت کرتا ہے وہ ماوراء اذھان پر کیونکر دال ہوسکتا ہے؟ وصفیت کی دوسری وجہ : لفظ اللہ وصف نہ ہو علم ہو تو اللہ عز شانہ کا ارشاد۔ اللہ نور السموات والارض کا معنی بغیر کسی تاویل کے صحیح نہ ہوگا بلکہ باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بر تقدیر علمیت آیت کا معنی ہوگا کہ ذات مشخص آسمان وزمین کا نور ہے جبکہ ذات وحدہ لاشریک کا آسمان میں ہونا بدلہبتہ باطل کہ وہ زمان ومکان سے منزہ اور مبرا ہے البتہ اگر وصف مانیں تو آیت متلوہ کے معنی میں کوئی فساد لازم نہیں آتا ہے اس لئے کہ اس تقدیر پر آیت کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ معبود آسمان وزمین کا نور ہے۔ وصفیت کی تیسری وجہ :۔ یہ ہے اس لفظ اور اسکے مبادی اشتقاق میں معنی اشتقاقی پایا جاتا ہے۔ معنی اشتقاقی موجود ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مشتق کا مشتق منہ کے لفظ اور معنی میں شریک ہونا ، چنانچہ لفظ اللہ کے جتنے ماخذ و مبادی تفسیر میں بیان کئے گئے ہیں ہر ایک مبدا کے ساتھ اس کو مناسبت نام حاصل ہے لہذا اس کا مشتق ہو نازیادہ ظاہر ہے وھو تعالی اعلم۔
The commentary 'Ashraf al-Nu'ut' explains that [the word 'Allah'] is a description, but it is such a description that is used predominantly only for the Essence of Allah; it cannot be applied to others. The conclusion is that it is a description that has become exclusive like a proper name. It is like 'Shari' and 'Sa'q' which are actually descriptions but due to predominant usage have become like proper names. Hence, just as a proper name is not an attribute but attributes are attached to it and no other share in it, similarly, no other will share in this word, but attributes will be attached to it as with a proper name. One reason for it being a description is that the Essence of Allah, in itself, disregarding real and relational attributes, is imperceptible in essence and inconceivable for humans. When His Essence is inconceivable, no word can denote His Essence, because words denote meanings in the mind, and the Essence transcends intellectual perception and mental representation. If a word were coined to denote His specific Essence, its indication would be possible, but it is false for any word to indicate His Essence because words indicate what is in the mind, while the referent of the word 'Allah' is beyond minds and intellects. So how can that which indicates what is in the mind indicate what is beyond minds? The second reason for its being a description: if the word 'Allah' were not a description but a proper name, then the meaning of Allah's statement 'Allahu nur al-samawati wa al-ard' would not be correct without interpretation but would be false. Because on the assumption of it being a proper name, the meaning of the verse would be that the specific essence is the light of the heavens and the earth, whereas it is necessarily false for the unique Essence to be in the heavens, as He is transcendent and free from time and place. However, if we take it as a description, then no corruption arises in the meaning of the recited verse, because on this assumption the meaning of the verse is that the object of worship is the light of the heavens and the earth. The third reason for its being a description: there is a derivational meaning between this word and its etymological origins. The presence of derivational meaning means that the derived word shares with the root in word and meaning. Thus, all the sources and origins of the word 'Allah' mentioned in exegesis have a relation of name with each origin; therefore, it is clearly derived. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic and theological analysis of the word 'Allah', presenting arguments for it being a descriptive attribute (sifah) rather than a proper name ('alam). The commentator follows the order of the author of the matn, addressing this issue. The first argument is epistemological: since Allah's essence is inconceivable, no word can directly denote it; therefore, 'Allah' must be a description pointing to an attribute. The second argument is theological: if it were a proper name, verses like 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth' would imply anthropomorphism, which is avoided by interpreting 'Allah' as 'the object of worship'. The third argument is linguistic: the word has derivational roots, indicating it is a derived description (ism mushtaq) rather than a primitive proper name. This discussion is typical of Hanafi usul where names of Allah are analyzed for their semantic and legal implications. The authority weight here is from the later scholarly tradition (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin) as this is a commentary on a classical text.

Key Terms
اللہ (Allah): A description of the divine Essence that has become like a proper name due to predominant usage.
وصف (sifah): An attribute or description that inheres in a subject, distinct from a proper name.
علم ('alam): A proper name that identifies a particular entity without conveying a meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it problematic to consider 'Allah' a proper name (علم)?
A) Because proper names cannot be used for Allah due to His transcendence.
B) Because it would lead to a literal interpretation of verses like 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth' implying spatial location.
C) Because proper names must have a clear etymological derivation.
D) Because the word 'Allah' is not used for any other being.

Key Takeaway
The word 'Allah' is a description (sifah) that has become exclusive through predominant usage, not a proper name, as proven by epistemological, theological, and linguistic arguments.

Definition of Ism Jins, Alam Jins, and the Hanafi Debate on Science Names
Defines noun types and debates classification of science names

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ism jins, alam jins, and alam shakhs, and evaluate the Hanafi dispute on whether names of sciences are common nouns or common proper nouns by analyzing the evidence of alif-lam, idafa, and mental unity.

Core Idea
Names of sciences are debated: alif-lam and idafa suggest common nouns, but mental unity suggests common proper nouns.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut defines three key noun classifications in Arabic—common noun, common proper noun, and personal proper noun—and then engages a central debate in Hanafi usul: are the names of sciences like nahw and fiqh common nouns (ism jins) or common proper nouns (alam jins)? Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi scholars reason from linguistic features to legal classifications.

Guided Path
1
Define the three noun types
List the definitions of ism jins, alam jins, and alam shakhs as given in the passage. Note the difference: ism jins applies to a universal or unspecified individual; alam jins has mental unity; alam shakhs is for a specific external person.
These definitions are foundational for the subsequent dispute.
2
Identify the dispute's core question
The debate: Are names of sciences (e.g., al-nahw, al-fiqh) common nouns (ism jins) or common proper nouns (alam jins)? The passage presents two positions and their evidence.
3
Analyze the evidence for ism jins
Some Hanafi scholars argue they are ism jins because these names take alif-lam (e.g., al-nahw) and allow idafa (e.g., Hidayah al-nahw). These features are characteristic of common nouns.
The author of Muslim al-Thubut prefers this view.
4
Examine objections and responses
Ibn al-Humam objects that compound idafa names like usul al-fiqh don't take alif-lam; the response broadens the evidence to simple names. Sayyid Zahid objects that alif-lam usage is a late innovation; the response cites celestial books (al-Qur'an, etc.) as counterexamples. A final response notes that alif-lam can enter descriptive proper nouns for beautification, weakening its exclusivity.
These objections and responses show the depth of Hanafi criticism and defense.
5
Evaluate the opposing view (alam jins)
Other Hanafi scholars argue that science names are alam jins because the named entity (the science) has mental unity (wahdat dhihniyya) and mental determination (ta'ayyun dhihni); e.g., 'fiqh' is a single reality in every scholar's mind. This mental unity is a defining feature of alam jins.
The passage ends with this argument, noting that if unity were not considered, applying 'fiqh' to different minds would be incorrect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۸۹
اسم جنس : ۔ اہل عربیہ کے نزدیک وہ اسم ہے جو نفس کلی من حیث ہی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور علما ، اصول کے نزدیک وہ اسم جو فرد منتشر غیر معین کے لئے موضوع ہو جیسے لفظ انسان اسم جنس ہے جو معنی کلی حیوان ناطق کے لئے یا اس کے فرد منتشر کے لئے موضوع ہے۔ علم جنس : وہ اسم ہے جو موضوع ہو ایسی شئی کے لئے جو صرف تعین ذہنی کے ساتھ متعین ہو یا جس میں وحدت ذہنیہ معتبر وملحوظ ہو جیسے لفظ اسامہ جو اس حقیقت اسد کے لئے موضوع ہے جس کے ساتھ وحدت ذہنیہ معتبر ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ ذہن میں اس کی حقیقت متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔
علم شخص : ۔ وہ اسم ہے جو شخص معین کے لئے موضوع ہو اپنے غیر سے ممتاز ہوذ ہن وخارج میں اس میں تکثر نہ ہو جیسے زید۔ متذکرہ بالا تعریفات ذہن نشین کر لینے کے بعد جان لینا چاہئے کہ بعض علمائے اصول کے نزد یک اسماء علوم و کتب اسماء جنس ہیں کیونکہ ان اسماء کے معانی کثیرین پر صادق آتے ہیں اور انکے معانی وہ علوم ہیں علماء کے اذھان کثیرہ میں موجود ثابت ہیں۔ یا پھر ان کے معانی وہ ملکات ہیں جو علماء کو حاصل ہوتے ہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ ان اسماء کی وضع یا تو طبائع کلیہ کے لئے ہوئی یا اس کے فرد غیر معین کے لئے ہوئی ہے بہر تقدیر یہ اسماء، اسماء جنس ہی قرار پائیں گے علم جنس یا علم مشخص نہیں ہو سکتے یہ ہب امام قاضی تاج الدین بیکی اور محمد بن امیر حاج کا ہے اور مصنف کا مختار ہے کہ اسکا اہم جنس ہو نازیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ وجه ظهور : یہ ہے کہ ان اسامی پر الف و لام داخل ہوتے ہیں اور اضافت ہوتی ہے چنانچہ النحو والصرف، ہدایۃ النحو مسلم الثبوت، اصول الفقہ وغیرھا بو لتے لکھتے ہیں اور الف ولام کا دخول اور اضافت کا لحوق اسماء جنس کے خواص میں سے ہے لہذا اسم جنس ہیں۔
ابن الهمام کا اعتراض : امام ابن الہمام نے تحریر میں یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ الف ولام اور اضافت کو اسم جنس ہونے کی علامت و خاصیت قرار دینا صحیح نہیں کیونکہ وہ اسماء علوم جو مرکب اضافی ہیں جیسے اصول الفقه ، ہدایۃ النحو وغیرھا خود اس پر الف ولام داخل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ الف لام تو صرف مفرد مثلا الاصول پر داخل ہوتا ہے اور یہ علم نہیں، رہے اصول الفقہ تو اس پر الف ولام نہیں ہے پھر اگر یہ دلیل اسم جنس ہونے پر تام بھی ہو جائے تو زیادہ سے زیادہ اصول الفقہ کا جنس ہونا ثابت ہوگا اس سے
دوسرے علوم کا جنس ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
جواب : بعض شارحین مسلم نے امام ابن الہام پر رد کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ ان کا یہ اعتراض اس وفقیت تام ہوگا جب خاص اصول الفقہ کے اسم جنس ہونے پر کلام کا مدار ہو حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہو بلکہ کلام تو مطلقاً اسامی علوم کے بارے میں ہے لہذا ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ مستدل کا مقصود یہ ہو کہ بعض علوم کے اسامی پر بحیثیت جنس الف ولام داخل ہوتے ہیں جیسے انو ، الصرف الفقہ وغیر ھا۔
سید زاهد كا اعتراض : سید زاہد ہروی نے یہاں یہ کلام کیا ہے کہ اسماء علوم الفلام کا دخول ان مولدین کے کلام میں حادث ہوا ہے جو فصاحت سے نابلد ہیں مگر وہ جو فصحاء ہیں تو ان کے کلام میں ایسا نہیں پایا جا تا ۔
جواب : یہ قول بھی مردود ہے اس لئے کہ اسماء کتب سماویہ جیسے القرآن، الانجیل الزبور، التوریت پر
الف ولام داخل ہے باوجود یکہ وہ کتابیں بالا جماع فصاحت و بلاغت کے حد اعجاز تک پہونچی ہوئی ہیں ۔ جواب باصواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ اسم جنس کے علاوہ اعلام وصفیہ پر بھی تحسین کے لئے لام کا دخول فصیح صحیح اور شائع و ذائع ہے چنانچہ حدیث شریف میں ہے الحسن والحسین سید اشباب اهل الجنة یونہی ادنی مناسبت کے سبب سے معنی علمیت باقی رکھتے ہوئے علم کی اضافت بھی صحیح ہے جیسے عمرنا او عمر الذى هو سيدنا وترجو مدده في كل حال من الاحوال - بلکہ اگر معنی علمیت سے خالی کر لیا جائے تو علم کے مضاف ہونے میں کوئی کلام ہی نہیں فلہذا دخول الف لام کا
اور لحوق اضافت دلیل جنسیت نہیں ہو سکتی۔ بعض علماء فن کا قول یہ ہے کہ اسماء علوم علم جنس ہیں اس لئے کہ علوم کے مسمیات یعنی مسائل و احکام کے مابین تعین ذہنی یا وحدت ذهنیہ معتبر ہے کیونکہ فقہ مثلا جب اس کو بہت سارے لوگ حاصل کرتے ہیں تو ان اشخاص کثیرہ میں سے ہر ایک کے ذہن میں جو ہے لامحالہ وہ فقہ ہی ہے پس اگر وحدت معتبر نہ ہو توان اشخاص کے ذہن میں جو علم ہے اس پر فقہ کا اطلاق صحیح نہ ہوگا چنانچہ اسی وجہ سے معلومات مخصوصہ کو علم مخصوص اور الفاظ مخصوصہ اور اس کے معانی کو کتاب مخصوص کہتے ہیں جس طرح ایک لفظ جود و شخص کی زبان سے صادر ہوا یا ایک ہی شخص سے دو وقتوں میں صادر ہوا یا ایک معنی جو دو ذھنوں میں حاصل ہے یا ایک ہی ذہن میں دو وقتوں میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو اسکو لفظ واحد
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut. 89. Common noun: According to Arabic linguists, it is a noun coined for the universal essence as such, and according to usul scholars, it is a noun coined for an unspecified distributed individual, like the word 'insan' (human) which is a common noun coined for the universal meaning of 'rational animal' or for its unspecified individual. Common proper noun: It is a noun coined for something that is determined only by mental determination, or in which mental unity is considered and observed, like the word 'Usamah' which is coined for the reality of 'lion' with which mental unity is considered; meaning that its reality becomes determined in the mind. Personal proper noun: It is a noun coined for a specific person, distinguished from others, and has no multiplicity in mind or reality, like 'Zayd'. After memorizing the above definitions, it should be known that according to some usul scholars, names of sciences and books are common nouns because their meanings apply to many individuals, and their meanings are those sciences that exist in the minds of many scholars, or they are dispositions that scholars acquire. In summary, their coinage is either for universal natures or for an unspecified individual. In any case, these names will be considered common nouns; they cannot be common proper nouns or personal proper nouns. This is the view of Imam Qadi Taj al-Din al-Bakki and Muhammad ibn Amir Haj, and the author's preferred view is that it is more apparent that it is a common noun. The evidence for its appearance is that alif-lam (the definite article) enters upon these names and they take idafa (construct state), as we say and write 'al-nahw, al-sarf, Hidayah al-nahw, Muslim al-thubut, usul al-fiqh', etc. The entry of alif-lam and the attachment of idafa are among the characteristics of common nouns, so they are common nouns. Ibn al-Humam's objection: Imam Ibn al-Humam objected in his writing that making alif-lam and idafa a sign and characteristic of being a common noun is not correct because those names of sciences that are compound idafa constructions, like 'usul al-fiqh' and 'Hidayah al-nahw', do not themselves receive alif-lam; rather, alif-lam only enters upon the singular, like 'al-usul', and that is not the science. As for 'usul al-fiqh', it does not have alif-lam. Then, even if this proof were complete for establishing being a common noun, at most it would prove that 'usul al-fiqh' is a common noun; from this the 'jinsiyya' (common noun status) of other sciences would not be proven. Answer: Some commentators on Muslim (al-Thubut) refuting Ibn al-Humam said that his objection would be perfectly valid only if the discussion focused specifically on 'usul al-fiqh' being a common noun, but such is not the case. Rather, the discussion is universally about the names of sciences. Therefore, it is possible that the arguer's intent is that on some names of sciences, by way of being common nouns, alif-lam enters, like 'al-nahw, al-sarf, al-fiqh', etc. Sayyid Zahid's objection: Sayyid Zahid Harawi stated here that the entry of alif-lam upon names of sciences occurred in the speech of later generations who are unfamiliar with eloquence, but as for the eloquent (classical) speakers, it is not found in their speech. Answer: This statement is also rejected because the names of celestial books, like 'al-Qur'an, al-Injil, al-Zabur, al-Tawrat', have alif-lam upon them, despite those books being unanimously at the peak of eloquence and rhetoric to the degree of inimitability. The correct answer: It is that besides common nouns, upon descriptive proper nouns, the entry of lam for beautification is eloquent, correct, and widespread. Thus, in the noble hadith: 'al-Hasan and al-Husayn are the leaders of the youth of Paradise.' Likewise, due to even a slight connection, while retaining the meaning of properness, idafa to 'ilm (science) is also correct, like 'Umaruna' or 'Umar alladhi huwa sayyiduna wa narju maddahu fi kulli hal min al-ahwal'. Rather, if the meaning of properness is removed, there is no objection to 'ilm being in idafa. Therefore, the entry of alif-lam and the attachment of idafa cannot be proof of jinsiyya (common noun status). Some scholars of the art say that names of sciences are common proper nouns because among the named entities, that is, the issues and rulings, mental determination or mental unity is considered. For example, when fiqh is acquired by many people, what is in the mind of each of these many individuals is inevitably that same fiqh. So if unity were not considered, the application of 'fiqh' to the knowledge in the minds of those individuals would not be correct. For this reason, specific known things are called 'specific knowledge' and specific words and their meanings are called 'specific book', just as a single word uttered by two individuals or by one individual at two times, or a single meaning present in two minds or in one mind at two times, is called a single word.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut, is a detailed discussion of the classification of nouns in Arabic, specifically the distinction between common nouns (ism jins), common proper nouns (alam jins), and personal proper nouns (alam shakhs), and their application to the names of sciences and books. The author begins by defining each term from both linguistic and usul perspectives. A common noun is a word coined for a universal essence or for an unspecified individual. A common proper noun is coined for something determined only in the mind, with mental unity. A personal proper noun is for a specific external person. The main argument concerns the names of sciences: some usul scholars argue they are common nouns because they accept the definite article (alif-lam) and are used in idafa (construct phrases). Evidence includes terms like al-nahw, al-sarf, and Hidayah al-nahw. Ibn al-Humam objects that compound idafa constructions like usul al-fiqh do not themselves take alif-lam; only the first part does. The response clarifies that the discussion is general, and alif-lam enters on simple names like al-nahw. Sayyid Zahid objects that such usage is late and not found in classical eloquent speech. The response cites celestial books (al-Qur'an, al-Injil, etc.) which have alif-lam and are the epitome of eloquence. A further refined response notes that alif-lam can enter descriptive proper nouns for beautification, and idafa can be retained with proper meaning, so these features are not exclusive to common nouns. Finally, some scholars hold that names of sciences are common proper nouns (alam jins) because the named entity (the science) has mental unity across individuals and times, thus requiring mental determination. The passage ends with an example: fiqh is a single entity in the mind of every scholar, so its name is a common proper noun. This debate is internal to Hanafi usul, with the author leaning toward the view that they are common nouns.

Key Terms
اسم جنس (ism jins): A noun coined for a universal essence or for an unspecified individual (fard muntashir); it applies to many instances without specifying one.
علم جنس (alam jins): A noun coined for something that is determined only by mental determination (ta'ayyun dhihni) and has mental unity; it is a proper noun for a class.
علم شخص (alam shakhs): A noun coined for a specific external person, distinguished from others, with no multiplicity in mind or reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence used by scholars who argue that names of sciences (like al-nahw, al-sarf) are common nouns (ism jins)?
A) These names are used for specific individuals.
B) These names accept alif-lam and idafa, which are characteristics of common nouns.
C) These names have mental determination and unity.
D) These names are found in the speech of the eloquent Arabs.

Key Takeaway
Names of sciences are a point of intra-Hanafi debate: their acceptance of alif-lam and idafa leans towards common nouns, but their mental unity suggests common proper nouns.

The Proof for Absolute Essence: Similarity and Circularity
Proof and critique of the reality of universals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the Hanafi proof for the external existence of absolute essences using a reductio ad absurdum, and evaluate the counter-argument of circularity.

Core Idea
If water droplets share real similarity, a common essence must exist externally—otherwise each would be a unique substance.

This passage presents a foundational philosophical argument in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the reality of universals. The author argues that since we observe similarity among individuals (e.g., drops of water), there must be a shared absolute essence existing in the external world. Without it, each individual would have a completely distinct essence, which contradicts their observed similarity. The passage then subjects this proof to a critical analysis, examining whether similarity can be interpreted in a way that avoids circularity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main thesis and reductio structure
State the author's thesis: absolute essence (māhiyya mutlaqa) exists externally. Then identify the reductio argument: if not, each water drop has a separate reality, violating the established fact of similarity (tamāthul) among substances.
The proof hinges on the principle that similar substances must share a common reality.
2
Examine the two formulations of the proof
Trace the first proof: existence of water individuals → question of shared reality → if affirmed, absolute essence is proven; if denied, each drop lacks components → leads to indivisibility and loss of effects, which is absurd. Trace the second proof: each drop is either essence+individual or only individuation; the latter leads to mutual separation of drops, contradicting established similarity.
Both formulations rely on the impossibility of denying similarity among water drops.
3
Analyze the objection: two interpretations of similarity
The commentator (likely al-Marginani) notes that the deniers of absolute essence interpret similarity as sharing in a particular attribute, not identity of essence. This allows distinct realities to share attributes without requiring a common essence.
If similarity means attribute-sharing, the reductio fails because drops can be similar without a shared essence.
4
Understand the circularity argument
Even if similarity is taken as identity, the proof fails: similarity itself must be proven, and its proof depends on the existence of absolute essence. Using similarity to prove absolute essence then becomes circular (dependence of a thing on itself).
This is a standard philosophical critique: the proof's premise (tamāthul) is not established independently.
5
Connect to Hanafi usul: implications for qiyas
The reality of universals underpins analogical reasoning (qiyas). If universals are only mental constructs, the transfer of rulings from the original case (asl) to the new case (far') based on a shared ʿilla becomes subjective. Hanafi commitment to objective universals ensures that legal analogy is grounded in external reality.
This debate directly affects the epistemological weight of qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.

اس کے برعکس کچھ علما فن کا یہ نظر یہ ہے کہ ماہیت مطلقہ خارج میں نہیں پائی جاتی ، خارج میں صرف اور صرف اشخاص موجود ہوتے ہیں جس کو ہو یت بسیطہ کہتے ہیں جن سے طبائع کلیہ عقلاً منتزع کئے جاتے ہیں اور یہ قوله فيه مافيه
دلیل مذکور کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ ہے چنانچہ مصنف نے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے ۔ " فيه مافيه فيه اشارة الى انه يجوز ان يكون معنى التماثل عند النافين هو الاشتراك في اخص وصف من الاوصاف اللازمة المنتزعة لا الاتحاد في الحقيقة المتحصلة ولوسلم فيجوز أن القول بالتماثل متفرعاً على القول بوجود الماهية المطلقة فاثباته يكون دوراً ، انتهت - ایراد کا حاصل یہ ہے تسلیم ہے کہ جواہر میں تماثل ثابت ہے لیکن تماثل جواہر سے اتحاد فی الحقیقۃ ثابت نہیں ہونا کیونکہ ماھیت مطلقہ کی نفی کرنے والوں کے نزدیک تماثل جواہر سے جواہر کے افراد کا اس کے اوصاف منتزعہ میں سے کسی وصف خاص میں اشتراک و تماثل مراد ہے اور تماثل فیما بین الوصف تباین حقائق کے منافی نہیں ، چنانچہ ایسا ہو سکتا کہ حقائق متبائن ہوں مگر کسی وصف خاص میں اشتراک و تماثل ہو اور اگر تسلیم ہی کر لیتے ہیں کہ تماثل جواہر سے اتحاد فی الحقیقہ ہی مراد ہے پھر بھی دلیل باطل ہوئی جاتی ہے اس لئے کہ قول ثبوت تماثل، ماهیت مطلقہ کے وجود کے قول پر متفرع ہے پس جب تک ماهیت مطلقہ خارج میں نہ پالی جائیگی اس وقت تک تماثل متفق نہیں ہو سکتا غرض تحقق تماثل، ماهیت مطلقہ کے وجود پر موقوف ہے پھر اگر ماهیت مطلقہ کا اثبات بھی تماثل ہی سے ہوتو دور کو مستلزم ہے کہ اس صورت میں تماثل موقوف علیہ ہوا جب کہ وہ موقوف تھا اور یہ تو قف اشی علی نفسہ ہے۔ یا یہ کہ تماثل جواہر کا اثبات بعینہ ماھیت مطلقہ کا اثبات ہے اور یہ اثبات الشی علی نفسہ ہے جو دور ہے اور دور محال اور جوستلزم محال وہ بھی محال لہذا تماثل جواہر کا قول محال ہو گیا۔

قوله اقول على طور الحكمة لانه لوكان الجزء حقا الخ خارج میں ماھیت مطلقہ کے وجود پر جو دلیل دی گئی ہے اس دلیل کی صحت چونکہ تماثل جواہر کے ثبوت پر موقوف تھی، اور تماثل جواہر سے خواہ اتحاد فی الحقیقة مراد لیں خواہ اشتراک فی الاوصاف، ہے دو تقدیر دلیل مذکور سے ماھیت مطلقہ کا ثبوت فراہم نہیں ہو پاتا ہے۔

اس لئے مصنف ماهمیت مطلقہ کے موجود ہونے پر تماثل جواہر ثابت کرتے ہوئے . ایک ایسی
In contrast, some scholars of the field hold that the absolute essence is not found in the external world; only individuals exist in the external world, which are called simple identities, from which universal natures are intellectually abstracted. These simple identities are in themselves distinct and individuated. Since simple individuations are those simple selves that do not share in any single reality that would be the substrate of multiple individuations. The author rejects this idea, saying: 'Otherwise, every drop of water would have a separate reality,' that is, if the absolute essence were not existent in the external world, then each and every drop of water would have a separate reality, and the consequent is false because the similarity of substances and their unity in reality is an established matter. Therefore, the similarity of substances is only possible if the existence of the absolute essence in the external world is admitted. Summary of the proof: The author's proof for the existence of the absolute essence is that simple bodies, such as the individuals of water, undoubtedly exist externally. Now the question is: is there a shared reality among these individuals of water or not? If affirmed, the existence of the absolute reality is proven. If denied, the question is: does each individual among all the individuals of water have matter, corporeal form, and the specific form of water? If they do, then each individual of water would have the reality of water, because reality is the body composed of matter, corporeal form, and specific form. And if in any individual of water, matter, corporeal form, and specific form are not found, then it would necessarily follow that no individual of water would be divisible, imaginary for the supposition of three dimensions, nor would it be capable of external effects, since the absence of corporeal and specific form has been assumed. And the necessary consequent is clearly false, so the antecedent is likewise. A second formulation of the proof: undoubtedly, drops of water exist externally. Then each of these drops either comprises both essence and individual, or comprises only individuation. On the first supposition, the desired is proven. On the second supposition, besides the fact that the distinguishing factor exists without the common factor, it also necessarily follows that each drop of water is mutually separated from the other, because individuations are mutually distinct in themselves, while the mutual separateness of each drop of water is clearly false, as the similarity and unity of substances is established and verified. 

[The author says:] There is something in it. This indicates the weakness of the mentioned proof. Thus the author said in the margin: 'There is something in it — it is an indication that it is possible that similarity according to the deniers is shared in the most specific of the necessary abstracted attributes, not unity in the achieved reality. And if accepted, it is possible that the statement of similarity is dependent on the statement of the existence of the absolute essence, so proving it would involve circularity.' End. The gist of the objection: It is admitted that similarity among substances is established, but the similarity of substances does not prove unity in reality, because for the deniers of the absolute essence, the similarity of substances means the sharing of the individuals of substances in a particular attribute among their abstracted attributes, and similarity among attributes is not contrary to the distinctness of realities. Thus it is possible that realities are distinct but share and are similar in a particular attribute. And even if we concede that similarity of substances means unity in reality, the proof is still invalid because the statement of the establishment of similarity is dependent on the statement of the existence of the absolute essence. So as long as the absolute essence is not found externally, similarity cannot be agreed upon. In short, the realization of similarity depends on the existence of the absolute essence. Then if the proof of the absolute essence also relies on similarity, circularity follows: in that case, similarity would be both the condition and the conditioned, which is the dependence of a thing on itself. Or it is that the proof of similarity is identical to the proof of the absolute essence, and this is proving a thing by itself, which is circularity, and circularity is impossible, and whatever entails impossibility is itself impossible. Hence, the statement of similarity becomes impossible. 

[The author says:] I say in the manner of wisdom: because if the part were true... etc. The proof given for the existence of the absolute essence in the external world, since its validity depended on the establishment of similarity of substances, and similarity of substances — whether taken as unity in reality or sharing in attributes — on both suppositions, the mentioned proof does not yield the proof of the absolute essence. Therefore, the author, while establishing the similarity of substances for the existence of the absolute essence, an such...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a philosophical argument concerning the existence of absolute essences (universals) in the external world, which is relevant to the Hanafi usul discussion on the reality of attributes and rulings. The author presents a proof by reductio: if absolute essences did not exist externally, then each water droplet would have its own unique essence. But this contradicts the established fact that substances (like water) are similar and share a common reality. Therefore, absolute essences must exist. The commentator then critiques this proof by noting that similarity can be interpreted as sharing in a particular attribute rather than identity of essence. Even if similarity is taken as identity, proving absolute essence via similarity would be circular because similarity itself depends on the existence of absolute essences. So the proof fails. The author then attempts to establish similarity of substances independently to avoid circularity. This is a classic debate between nominalists (deniers of universals) and realists (affirmers), but within an Islamic philosophical-theological context. The Hanafi school generally affirms the reality of universals as basis for legal analogies and classifications.

Key Terms
ماہیت مطلقہ (māhiyya mutlaqa): The absolute essence or universal nature that is shared among individuals, existing externally.
تماثل (tamāthul): Similarity or equality among substances in their essential reality or attributes.
تشخص (tashakhkhus): Individuation; that which makes an individual distinct from others of the same species.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the critique claim that the author's proof is circular?
A) Because the proof uses the concept of water, which is itself a universal.
B) Because similarity (tamāthul) is used to prove absolute essence, but similarity itself depends on absolute essence.
C) Because water drops are known to be identical, not just similar.
D) Because the author's proof is based on a logical fallacy.

Key Takeaway
The reality of universals is necessary for the validity of analogical reasoning in Hanafi fiqh, but establishing it requires overcoming the challenge of circularity.

Refuting Indivisible Parts: A Geometric Proof in Usul al-Fiqh
Geometric proof refuting indivisible atoms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi geometric argument against indivisible parts and identify how it demonstrates the continuity of matter.

Core Idea
If indivisible atoms existed, basic geometry would contradict itself — therefore, matter must be continuous.

This passage presents a rational proof from geometry used by Hanafi-Maturidi scholars to refute the existence of indivisible parts (atomism), a position held by some mutakallimun. By applying the Pythagorean theorem and triangle inequality to a hypothetical right triangle composed of indivisible units, the author demonstrates that such a model leads to an impossible conclusion. Understanding this proof strengthens your grasp of how aqli (rational) dalil is employed in usul al-fiqh to support metaphysical positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Thesis
The passage aims to prove that indivisible parts (juz' alladhi la yatajazza) are false. Recognize this as the conclusion to be established.
The thesis is explicitly stated: 'The similarity of atoms is established, so the indivisible part is false.'
2
Understand the Geometric Premises
Two geometric claims are used: (1) The 'Himari form' (triangle inequality) states that the sum of any two sides of a triangle is greater than the third. (2) The 'Arusi form' (Pythagorean theorem) states that the square of the hypotenuse of a right triangle is greater than the square of each side.
These are assumed as self-evident truths (musallamat).
3
Set Up the Hypothetical
Assume indivisible parts exist. Consider a right triangle where each side (the two legs) is composed of exactly two indivisible parts each. Since one part is shared at the right angle, the total parts in the two legs sum to three (2+2-1=3).
The shared part is crucial for the arithmetic.
4
Apply the Premises to Derive Contradictions
Apply the Himari form: The hypotenuse must be less than the sum of the two legs (which is three parts), so it cannot be three parts. Apply the Arusi form: The hypotenuse must be greater than each leg (each two parts), so it cannot be two parts. Therefore, the hypotenuse must be between two and three parts.
This forces the hypotenuse to be a non-integer number of parts, implying division of the assumed indivisible parts.
5
Conclude the Impossibility
Since the hypotenuse must be a fractional number of parts, the assumption of indivisible parts leads to a contradiction. Thus, indivisible parts cannot exist, and matter must be infinitely divisible (continuous). This establishes tamathul al-jawahir (similarity of atoms).
The proof concludes: 'Thus division is necessitated, so its being an indivisible part becomes invalid.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قائمہ کے وتر کا مربع اس کے دونوں ضلعوں کے مربع کے مجموعہ کے برابر ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہ فرض کیا جائے کہ اس کا ہر ضلع دو جزء کا ہے تو اس کا لازمی نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ وتر دوجز سے بڑا ہو گا ور نہ عروسی کا دعوی باطل ہو جائے گا۔
حاصل دلیل : ۔ یہ ہے کہ تماثل جواہر ثابت ہے پس جزء الذی لا تجر می باطل ہے کیونکہ جز و الذی لاس تخمیری اگر باطل نہ ہو بلکہ موجود ثابت ہو جیسا کہ متکلمین کہتے ہیں تو ہم کہیں گے کہ ایک زاویہ قائمہ فرض کیا جائے جس کا ہر ضلع دو جز کا ہوگا اور دونوں ضلعوں کا مجموعہ تین اجزاء کے ہوں گے کیونکہ جز واحد دونوں ضلعوں میں مشترک ہے لہذ از اویہ قائمہ کا وتر تین جز کا نہیں ہوسکتا۔ کیونکہ شکل حماری کا دعوی یہ ہے کہ مثلث کے دو ضلع کا مجموعہ وتر سے بڑا ہوتا ہے، پس جب دونوں ضلع کا مجموعہ تین اجزاء کے ہوئے تو ظاہر ہے کہ وتر تین اجزاء سے کم کا ہوگا ورنہ حماری کا دعویٰ مسلمہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح و تر دو جز کا بھی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ شکل عروسی کا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ زاویہ قائمہ والے مثلث کا وتر کا مربع مثلث کے ہر ایک ضلع کے مربع سے بڑا ہوتا ہے، چونکہ مثلث کا ہر ضلع دو جز کا ہے اور اس کا مربع چار ہے تو ظاہر کہ وتر دو جز سے بڑا ہوگا تا کہ اس کا مربع ہر ضلع کے مربع سے بڑا ہو ورنہ شکل عروسی کا دعوئی مسلمہ باطل ہو جائے گا، الغرض مثلث کا وتر تین جزء کا ہوانہ دو جز کا بلکہ تین اور دو کے درمیان ہوالہذ ا انقسام ہو گیا جزئیت باطل ہوگئی اور جب جزئیت باطل ٹھہری تو اتصال ثابت ہو گیا کہ جسم جو ہر متصل ممتد پر مشتمل ہوتا ہے جس کو صورت جسمیہ کہتے ہیں، پھر یہی جسم ممتد متصل ان اجزاء کی طرف منقسم ہوتا ہے جو آپس میں متماثل اور حقیقت میں متحد ہوتے ہیں پس اجزائے جسم من حیث الحقیقہ متحد ہوئے کیونکہ دو متبائن حقیقت جیسے عناصر اربعہ باہم متصل نہیں ہوتے بلکہ زیادہ سے زیادہ مماس ہوتے ہیں جیسا کہ ابن سینا نے کہا ہے۔
اور جب زیر بحث مسئلہ میں اجزاء مماس نہیں ہیں بلکہ متصل ہیں تو تماثل جواہر ثابت ہوا پھر جب تماثل ہو گیا تو ماهیت مطلقہ کا وجود خارجی بھی ثابت ہو گیا کہ ماھیت مطلقہ کا ثبوت تماثل جواہر پر موقوف تھا۔ اس مفہوم کو مصنف نے ایک طویل حاشیہ میں بیان کیا ہے۔
توضيحه أن الجز الذى لا يتجزى لو كان حقا فليفرض قائمة كل خط منها جز أن فالمجموع ثلثة لان الجزء الواحد مشترك بين الخطين وح نقول أن الوتر هو الخط الواصل بين الخطين لا يكون مركبا من ثلثة اجزاء بالشكل الحمارى لان دعواه أن مجموع الضلعين من المثلث اى ضلعين كانا اعظم من الثالث فههنا حصل بالوتر مثلث فكل ضلعين من القائمة يجب أن يكون اقل من الثالث وقد فرض أن الضلعين ثلثة اجزاء فلو كان الوتر ايضا ثلثة اجزاء لزم المساوات وذالك باطل فح يجب ان يكون اقل من ثلثة... ولا يكون ايضا مركباً من جزئين بالشكل العروسى لانه قد ثبت به أن وتر القائمة ازيد من كل واحد من الضلعين وقد فرض أن كل من الضلعين مركب من جزئين فلو كان الوتر ايضاً كذالك لزم المساوات وذالك باطل فح يجب ان يكون اقل من مجموع الجزئين فلايجوز أن يكون الوتر ثلثة اجزاء ولا اثنين بل يجب ان يكون بين الثلاثة والاثنين فيلزم الانقسام لانه وجد الاقل من الجزء فبطل كونه جزء الذي لايتجزى انتهت
The square of the hypotenuse of a right triangle equals the sum of the squares of its two sides. And if it is assumed that each of its sides is two parts, then the necessary result is that the hypotenuse will be greater than two parts, otherwise the claim of al-Arusi would become false.
Summary of the proof: The similarity of atoms is established, so the indivisible part is false. Because if the indivisible part is not false but rather exists, as the theologians say, then we would say: assume a right triangle each of whose sides is two parts, and the sum of the two sides will be three parts because one part is shared between the two sides. Therefore we say that the hypotenuse, which is the line connecting the two sides, cannot be composed of three parts according to the Himari form. Because his claim is that the sum of the two sides of a triangle, whichever two sides, is greater than the third. So here a triangle is formed with the hypotenuse. For any two sides of a right triangle, their sum must be less than the third. And we have assumed the two sides are three parts. So if the hypotenuse were also three parts, equality would result, and that is false. Therefore it must be less than three parts. And it also cannot be composed of two parts according to the Arusi form. Because it is established by him that the hypotenuse of a right triangle is greater than each of the two sides. And we have assumed that each of the two sides is composed of two parts. So if the hypotenuse were also like that, equality would result, and that is false. Therefore it must be less than the sum of the two parts. So the hypotenuse cannot be three parts nor two, but must be between three and two. Thus division is necessitated, because something less than a part is found, so its being an indivisible part becomes invalid. End.
And when it is established that the parts are not contiguous but rather continuous, then the similarity of atoms is established. Then when similarity is established, the external existence of absolute quiddity is also established, because the proof of absolute quiddity depends on the similarity of atoms. The author has explained this meaning in a long footnote.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a detailed rational proof from geometry aimed at refuting the existence of indivisible atoms (juz' alladhi la yatajazza), a position held by some mutakallimun (theologians). The author, following the Hanafi-Maturidi tradition, argues that if atoms were truly indivisible, fundamental geometric principles such as the Pythagorean theorem would be violated. By assuming a right triangle with sides composed of two indivisible parts each, and using the claims of two geometric forms (Himari and Arusi), he shows that the hypotenuse would have to be neither three nor two parts, forcing an intermediate division, thus proving that parts must be further divisible. This establishes the continuous nature of matter and supports the Hanafi position on the similarity of atoms (tamathul al-jawahir) and the external existence of absolute quiddity.

Key Terms
جزء الذی لا یتجزأ (juz' alladhi la yatajazza): An indivisible part or atom that cannot be further divided
تماثل جواہر (tamathul al-jawahir): The similarity/sameness of all individual atoms in their essence
شکل حماری (shakl himari): A form of geometric proof attributed to Himari, probably referring to the triangle inequality
شکل عروسی (shakl arusi): A form of geometric proof attributed to Arusi, probably the Pythagorean theorem

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the geometric argument, what is the necessary conclusion about the hypotenuse of a right triangle with legs of two indivisible parts each (sharing one part at the vertex)?
A) The hypotenuse must be exactly three parts.
B) The hypotenuse must be exactly two parts.
C) The hypotenuse must be between two and three parts, proving division.
D) The hypotenuse cannot be determined.

Key Takeaway
Rational geometric proof demonstrates that the assumption of indivisible atoms leads to a logical contradiction, thereby confirming the Hanafi-Maturidi view of the continuity of matter.

Definition and Properties of Dhati (Essential Predicate) in Hanafi Usul
Definition of dhati with properties and critique of alternative definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three properties of dhati and distinguish it from necessary accidents according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Dhati is the core part of the essence without which the essence cannot be conceived, and its existence is self-caused.

In Hanafi usul, precise definitions are critical for deriving rulings. This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut defines dhati (essential predicate), enumerates its three properties, and refutes a broader definition. Understanding dhati is key to constructing valid definitions (hudud) of fiqh terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
The passage defines 'dhati' in the context of Hanafi usul and logic. Note that the majority restrict dhati to the part of the essence that is predicated on the essence.
2
Enumerate the three properties of dhati
List each property: (1) conceptual inseparability, (2) self-causation, (3) impossibility of removal. Understand the meaning of each.
3
Distinguish dhati from necessary accident
The passage raises a doubt and refutes it. Dhati is constitutive of the essence, while 'arad lazim depends on the essence.
4
Analyze the alternative definition 'ma la yu'allal'
This definition is critiqued as too broad, including accidental attributes like possibility and existence. Understand why it is weak.
5
Reach the preferred definition
The author and Ibn al-Hajib (according to the text) both adhere to the definition based on the first property. Recognize the tarjih.

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۱۳۲
ذات پر بھی شائع ہے جیسا کہ ابن سینا نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے البتہ جمہور نے ذاتی کو جزء ماھیت کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا ہے وہ بھی مطلق جزء ماهیت کو ذاتی نہیں کہتے بلکہ وہ جز ء جو ماھیت پر محمول ہوتی ہو ذاتی کہلاتی ہے اسلئے بر بنائے مذہب جمہور شئی کے اجزاء خارجیہ ذاتی نہ ہونگے کہ اجزاء خارجیہ ماهیت پر محمول نہیں ہوتے ۔
ذاتی ہونے کے خواص :۔ یاد رکھو کہ ذاتی کے تین خواص ہوتے ہیں۔
(۱) ذات کا تصور بغیر تصور ذاتی محال اور ممتنع ہے۔
(۲) ذاتی کا ثبوت ذات کے لئے لذاتہ ہوتا ہے یعنی ذاتی اپنے ثبوت و وجود میں سوائے علت ذات کے کسی دوسری علت کی محتاج نہیں ہوتی ۔ چنانچہ سواد لذا تہ لون ہے، ایسا نہیں کہ کسی شئی آخر نے
سواد کولون بنا دیا ہے بلکہ جس چیز نے سواد کو سواد بنایا ہے اسی نے سواد کولون بنایا ہے۔ (۳) ذاتی کا رفع اس چیز سے جس کی وہ ذاتی ہے وجود و تو ہم دونوں لحاظ میں ممتنع ہے۔ شبہ :۔ یہاں یہ شبہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ذاتی کے ذکر کردہ دو خاصوں میں بعض لوازم عرضیہ بھی مشترک ہیں مثلا اثنین زوجیت کے ساتھ متصف ہونے میں سوائے علت ذات کے دوسری طرف محتاج نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اس طرح زوجیت کا رفع اثنین سے وجود و تو ھم دونوں لحاظ میں ناممکن ہے ۔ حالانکہ یہ ذاتی کا خاصہ ہے۔ دفع : ۔ ذاتی کے خاصہ میں اگر چہ لوازم عرضیہ شریک ہورہے ہیں تاہم مضر نہیں ۔ اس لئے کہ ذاتی اور عرض لازم کے درمیان بڑا فرق ہے۔ کہ ذاتی اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کی طرف ذات محتاج ہو چونکہ ذاتی ماهیت کا جز اور اس کا مقوم ہوتی ہے اس کے برعکس عرض لا زم وہ ہے جو خود ماهیت وذات کی طرف محتاج ہو۔ پھر بھی مصنف نے ذاتی کی تعریف ذاتی کے مندرجہ بالا تینوں خاصوں میں سے خاصہ اولیٰ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے کی ہے جس میں کوئی لوازم خارجیہ ذاتی کے شریک نہیں ہے۔ مگر دوسرے مصنفین نے ذاتی کے تینوں خاصوں کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے تعریف کی ہے اس لئے وہ تعریف جس کو مصنف نے بیان کیا ہے وہ بھی ذکر کئے ہیں اور اس کے علاوہ بھی ذکر کئے ہیں اس کی کئی وجھیں ہیں۔ تاکہ ذاتی کے تینوں خاصوں کی طرف تنبیہ ہو جائے۔ یا اشارہ ہو جائے کہ ذاتی کی تعریف تینوں خاصوں میں سے کسی سے بھی جائز ہے یا پھر تغییر مذکور سے مضر ذاتی کے حکم کا اثبات مقصود
ہو وغیرہ ۔ جیسا کہ ابن حاجب نے مختصر میں کہا ہے اس طرف مصنف نے اشارہ کیا اپنے قول مالا یعلل ہے ۔ قوله - مالایعلل الخ۔ یہ ذاتی کی دوسری تعریف ہے جو علامہ ابن حاجب نے مختصر میں ذکر کیا ہے اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جس کا ثبوت ذات کے لئے بغیر علت کے ہو یا جس کا ثبوت ذات کے لئے سوائے علت ذات کے کسی علت کا محتاج نہ ہو وہ شئی کی ذاتی کہلاتی ہے (اسی بنا پر کہا جاتا ہے کہ مجعولیت ذاتیہ محال ہے ) ماتن کے نزدیک یہ تعریف ضعیف ہے اس لئے "قیل" سے تعبیر کیا اور پھر ينقض بالا مکان سے اس تعریف پر اعتراض وارد کیا۔
اعتراض کی تقریر :۔ یہ ہے کہ ذاتی کی تعریف امکان ، وجود وغیرہ ان اعراض سے ٹوٹ رہی ہے جو اعراض مرتبہ ذات میں موجود ہوتے ہیں بلفظ دیگر یہ تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہیں کہ یہ تعریف امکان و وجود وغیرہ اعراض پر صادق آرہی ہے اس لئے کہ امکان بھی ممکن کے لئے بغیر علت ثابت ہے حالانکہ امکان ممکن کے لئے ذاتی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے لوازم میں ہے۔ لہذا ذاتی اور اس قسم کی عرضی جیسے امکان وجود اور وہ تمام اعراض جو مرتبہ ذات میں موجود ہوتے ہیں کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہ رہا
کیونکہ امکان وجود وغیرہ بھی بلاریب اعراض ہیں باوجود اس کے ذاتی کی تعریف اس عرضی پر صادق آرہی ہے۔ جواب : حق یہ ہے کہ علامہ ابن حاجب پر یہ اعراض وارد نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ذاتی کی تعریف انہوں نے بھی وہی کی ہے جو مصنف نے کی ہے البتہ جنہوں نے ذاتی کی تعریف مالا یعلل سے کی ہے اس تعریف کو علامہ نے نقل کر دی ہے اور اس کے ضعف کی طرف انہوں نے بھی ویسے ہی اشارہ کیا ہے جیسا کہ مصنف نے اشارہ کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ختصر میں ہے۔
والذاتي مالا يتصور فهم الذات قبل فهمه كاللونية للسواد والجسمية
للانسان ومن ثم لم يكن لشئى حد ان ذاتيان وقد يعرف بانه غير معلل وبالترتيب
العملى انتهت
اس عبارت سے بہت ظاہر ہے کہ علامہ کے نزدیک ذاتی کی وہی تعریف صواب ہے جو مصنف کے نزدیک ہے اور غیر معلل سے ذاتی کی تعریف ان کے نزدیک بھی مرجوح ہے اس لئے ان کی طرف انتساب کسی طرح درست نہیں۔ پھر بھی ہم کہیں گے کے غیر معلل سے ذاتی کی تعریف نہیں
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut. 132. It is also prevalent on the essence, as Ibn Sina has clarified. However, the majority (jumhur) have restricted dhati to the part of the essence (juz' mahiyyah), and they do not call any part of the essence dhati, but rather the part that is predicated on the essence is called dhati. Therefore, according to the majority's school, the external parts of a thing are not dhati because external parts are not predicated on the essence. Properties of being dhati: Remember that dhati has three properties: (1) It is impossible and inconceivable to imagine the essence without imagining the dhati. (2) The establishment of dhati for the essence is by itself (li-dhatihi), i.e., dhati in its establishment and existence does not need any other cause besides the cause of the essence. For example, blackness is color by itself; it is not that something else made blackness a color, but rather the thing that made blackness black also made it color. (3) The removal of dhati from that of which it is a dhati is impossible both in existence and in imagination. Doubt: Here a doubt can arise that some accidental necessary concomitants (lawazim 'aradiyya) also share the two mentioned properties. For example, the number two in being characterized by evenness does not need any other cause besides the cause of the essence. Similarly, the removal of evenness from two is impossible both in existence and imagination. Yet this is a property of dhati. Refutation: Although accidental necessary concomitants share in the property of dhati, it is not harmful because there is a big difference between dhati and necessary accident: dhati is that which the essence needs, because dhati is part of the essence and its constituent; on the contrary, necessary accident is that which itself needs the essence and the self. Nevertheless, the author (Musannif) defined dhati by looking at the first of the three properties mentioned above, in which no external necessary concomitants share with dhati. But other authors looked at all three properties, so they have mentioned the definition that the author stated and also others for several reasons: to draw attention to the three properties, or to indicate that the definition of dhati from any of the three properties is permissible, or to establish the ruling of dhati through the mentioned change, etc. As Ibn Hajib said in al-Mukhtasar, the author indicated this by his statement 'ma la yu'allal'. His statement 'ma la yu'allal' etc. is the second definition of dhati that Allama Ibn Hajib mentioned in al-Mukhtasar. Its gist is that that whose establishment for the essence is without cause, or whose establishment for the essence does not need any cause besides the cause of the essence, is called dhati of that thing. (On this basis it is said that the made-ness of dhati is impossible.) According to the author (matn), this definition is weak, therefore he expressed it with 'qila' (it was said) and then he objected to this definition with 'yantaqidu bi al-makan' (it is refuted by place). Explanation of the objection: This definition is broken by such accidents as possibility, existence, etc., which exist in the order of the essence. In other words, this definition does not prevent the entry of other things, because this definition applies to possibility, existence, etc. For possibility is also established for the possible without cause, although possibility is not dhati for the possible but rather among its necessary concomitants. Hence no difference remains between dhati and this kind of accidents such as possibility, existence, and all the accidents that exist in the order of essence. Because possibility, existence, etc. are undoubtedly accidents, yet the definition of dhati applies to them. Response: The truth is that this objection does not apply to Allama Ibn Hajib, because his definition of dhati is the same as the author's. However, he transmitted the definition of dhati from those who defined it as 'ma la yu'allal' and he also indicated its weakness just as the author indicated. In al-Mukhtasar it says: 'And dhati is that whose understanding of the essence cannot be imagined before understanding it, like colorness for blackness and bodyness for man, and hence nothing has a definition unless it has two dhatis. And it may be defined as uncaused (ghayr mu'allal) and by the practical arrangement.' End. From this expression it is very clear that according to Allama, the correct definition of dhati is the same as according to the author, and the definition by 'ghayr mu'allal' is also preponderated (marjuh) according to him. Therefore, attributing (the weak definition) to him is not correct in any way. Still, we will say that the definition of dhati by 'ghayr mu'allal' is not...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a technical discussion defining the term 'dhati' (essential predicate) within the framework of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, drawing on logic (mantiq). The author begins by noting a broader definition by Ibn Sina but then adopts the majority (jumhur) view that dhati is specifically the part of the essence (mahiyya) that is predicated on the essence itself, not external parts. Three essential properties of dhati are enumerated: first, the essence cannot be conceived without it; second, its existence for the essence is self-caused (li-dhatihi), requiring no external cause; third, its removal from the essence is impossible both in reality and in thought. A doubt is raised that some accidental necessary attributes (like evenness for the number two) share these properties, but the refutation clarifies that the key difference is that dhati is constitutive of the essence (juz' wa muqawwim), whereas a necessary accident is dependent on the essence. The author then critiques a secondary definition of dhati as 'ma la yu'allal' (uncaused) attributed to Ibn al-Hajib, arguing that this definition is too broad and includes accidental attributes like possibility and existence. The commentary shows that the true definition according to the author (and also Ibn al-Hajib himself, according to the text) is the first one based on the first property: that dhati is that without which the essence cannot be understood. The passage exemplifies the Hanafi method of precise conceptual analysis in usul al-fiqh, ensuring that technical terms are rigorously distinguished.

Key Terms
ذاتی (dhati): That part of the essence (mahiyya) which is predicated on the essence and without which the essence cannot be understood; it has three specific properties and is constitutive of the thing.
عرض لازم ('arad lazim): A necessary accident that is inseparable from the essence but not constitutive of it; it depends on the essence rather than the essence depending on it.
ماهیت (mahiyya): The essence or quiddity of a thing; what it is in itself, composed of its essential parts (dhawati).
علت ذات ('illat al-dhat): The cause of the essence itself, i.e., the reason that makes the essence what it is; dhati has no cause other than this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a property of dhati (essential predicate)?
A) It is caused by something external to the essence.
B) Its removal from the essence is impossible both in reality and in thought.
C) It is a necessary accident that depends on the essence.
D) It is an external part of the thing that is not predicated on the essence.

Key Takeaway
Dhati is the part of the essence without which the essence cannot be understood and whose existence is self-caused; it must be distinguished from necessary accidents that depend on the essence.
