جواب کے ضعف کی دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس بحث میں مقصود قضیہ حملیہ ہے اور وہ ہمارا قول ثبوت استحقاق الجزاء لا فعال معلوم عقلا ہے، لہذ ا مطلوب کے اثبات میں مستدل نے قضیہ شرطیہ پیش کی ہے کافی نہیں ، اس لئے کہ ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ شرط بھی پائی ہی نہ جائے جب تو تالی بھی کبھی نہ پائی جائیگی اس تقدیر پر مطلوب کبھی ثابت نہ ہو سکے گا اس لئے مقدم کے تحقیق و وضع کا علم ضروری ہے تا کہ اس کے علم سے تالی کا علم ہو سکے اگر مقدم کا علم سمعا ہوا تو تالی کا علم سمعا ہوگا اگر عقلاً ہوا تو تالی کا علم بھی عقلا ہو گا لیکن ایسا ممکن ہے کہ وضع مقدم کا علم سمعی ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ وضع تالی کا علم بھی سمعی ہی ہو گا جب تو تالی کا تحقق عقل کبھی نہیں ہوسکتا لہذا یہ جواب نا کافی ہے۔
The commentary on Muslim al-Thubut: near, not prohibited. Summary: Fadil Mirza Jan meant by his statement 'the matter of the Hereafter is sam‘i' that absolutely the matter of the Hereafter is sam‘i, but this is prohibited because philosophers do not absolutely deny the Hereafter; rather, they specifically deny bodily resurrection, and they rationally consider spiritual resurrection permissible. Thus Shaykh al-Ra’is said in his book al-Shifa, chapter 'al-Mafad min al-Ilahiyyat': 'Among them is what is known from the Sharia, with no way to prove it except through the Sharia and belief in prophetic news, and that is bodily resurrection. And among them is what the intellect has a way to perceive, and that is spiritual resurrection and what the soul experiences of pleasure and pain after separation from the body.' The gist is that bodily resurrection cannot be perceived rationally, but spiritual resurrection can be perceived by reason. So if absolutely and in every respect the matter of the Hereafter were sam‘i, then why would philosophers—heretics who deny the Hereafter—admit spiritual resurrection? Therefore it must be admitted that the matter of the Hereafter is not sam‘i in every respect. And if Fadil Mirza Jan meant by his statement 'the matter of the Hereafter is sam‘i' that bodily resurrection is sam‘i, then this is true and correct, but it is not harmful to the Mu‘tazila, because for reward and punishment, the absolute existence of the abode of recompense is sufficient, even if spiritual resurrection is correct. Thus it passed from the shaykh’s citation that among the benefits of the divine is that which the intellect can perceive, and that is spiritual resurrection, and it is the soul that after separation from the body feels pleasure and pain. His statement: 'on condition that it means: if it exists then it is sufficient, etc.' From the above expression, a second answer to Fadil Mirza Jan’s objection is given. The gist of the answer is that the Mu‘tazila’s statement 'and from it is that which is necessary' is in the sense of true investigation, whose import is that if the matter of the Hereafter and the abode of recompense exist, then the deserving of reward and punishment will also exist. So those who claim that some good and evil are self-evident mean by this that if the abode of recompense exists, then according to reason the doer of a good act deserves reward and the committer of an evil act deserves punishment. In short, reason necessarily judges the existence of the second given the estimation of the first, because for reason to judge the self-evidence of good and evil, this meaning is sufficient; it is not dependent on the arrival of revelation. His statement: 'then contemplate' indicates the weakness of the mentioned answer. The reason for weakness is that this answer is of the type of 'justifying a statement with what the speaker does not approve', because this meaning of the goodness of an act and the evil of an act has not been transmitted from any of them. The second reason for the weakness of the answer is that in this discussion the intended proposition is categorical, and it is our statement: 'the proof of the deserving of recompense for actions is known rationally'. Therefore, to prove what is sought, the arguer presented a conditional proposition, which is insufficient, because it is possible that the condition may not exist at all, so then the consequent may never exist. On this assumption, what is sought can never be proven. Hence knowledge of the verification and positing of the antecedent is necessary so that from its knowledge the knowledge of the consequent can be obtained. If the knowledge of the antecedent is by revelation, then the knowledge of the consequent will be by revelation; if it is rational, then the knowledge of the consequent will also be rational. But it is possible that the knowledge of the positing of the antecedent is by revelation, then it is clear that the knowledge of the positing of the consequent will also be by revelation, so then reason can never realize the consequent. Therefore, this answer is insufficient.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute regarding the epistemological source of matters of the Hereafter. The commentator refutes Fadil Mirza Jan's claim that all matters of the Hereafter are known solely through revelation (sam‘i). The refutation proceeds by pointing out that philosophers (falasifa) affirm spiritual resurrection (ma‘ad ruhani) through reason, while only bodily resurrection (ma‘ad jismani) is known exclusively through revelation. The commentator cites Ibn Sina from al-Shifa to support this distinction. Then, the conditional argument of the Mu‘tazila is examined: they argue that if the abode of recompense exists, then reason necessarily mandates reward and punishment. The commentator points out two weaknesses: first, this answer misrepresents the opponent's view by attributing a meaning not intended; second, the argument uses a conditional proposition (qadiyya shartiyya) whereas the dispute is about a categorical proposition (qadiyya hamliyya), making the argument insufficient because the condition might never be fulfilled. Thus, the passage concludes that such reasoning fails to establish the rational necessity of reward and punishment without revelation.

Key Terms
سمعي (sam‘ī): Known only through revelation (Quran and Sunnah), not through reason.
عقلي (‘aqlī): Known through reason independently of revelation.
معاد جسماني (ma‘ād jismānī): Bodily resurrection, which is sam‘ī.
معاد روحاني (ma‘ād rūḥānī): Spiritual resurrection of the soul, which is ‘aqlī.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of resurrection is known only through revelation (sam‘ī)?
A) Spiritual resurrection (ma‘ād rūḥānī)
B) Bodily resurrection (ma‘ād jismānī)
C) Both types
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection is known only through revelation (sam‘ī), but spiritual resurrection and its rational implications are accessible to reason (‘aqlī).

Can Reason Alone Make Faith Obligatory? The Hanafi Dispute on Reason's Independence
Expanding on a intra-Hanafi usul dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minority and majority Hanafi positions on reason's independence in determining rulings, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to the case of a person without revelation.

Core Idea
Reason knows good and evil, but majority Hanafis hold that obligation comes only from divine command, not reason alone.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a subtle but important dispute: Can reason independently impose the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief, even without revelation? While most Hanafis agree with the Mu'tazila that good and evil are rationally known, they draw the line at making reason a direct source of obligation. The minority view, attributed to some Hanafis (and Mu'tazila), claims that in some cases, reason alone can necessitate a ruling. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the matn and commentary to distinguish between the minority Hanafi view (reason is independent in some rulings) and the majority Hanafi view (reason knows good/evil but does not create obligation).
The minority view is attributed to 'some Hanafis' and also to Mu'tazila.
2
Analyze the key point of divergence
The commentary states that good and evil (husn/qubh) are known by reason, but for the majority, they are only a cause for preponderance (illat al-tarjih), not a necessitation (istilzam). The minority holds that good 'temporarily necessitates' a ruling (husn 'aradi mustalzim hukm).
Understand the difference: cause for preponderance vs. necessitation.
3
Interpret the Abu Hanifa narration
The matn quotes Abu Hanifa: 'No one has any excuse for ignorance of his Creator, because he sees clear proofs.' The commentator interprets this as applying after a period of reflection, not as an immediate rational obligation.
This interpretation harmonizes the narration with the majority view.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is the case of a person who reaches puberty on a mountain peak with no access to revelation. The minority would hold that reason alone obligates faith; the majority would say no obligation until revelation reaches them.
This is a classic problem in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator does not explicitly choose, but the structure favors the majority view by distinguishing knowledge from obligation. The minority view is presented neutrally.
The text leaves the final tarjih open, but the majority view is implied.

متن المسلم : ثم من الحنفية من قال ان العقل قد يستقل في ادراك بعض احكامه تعالى فاوجب الايمان وحرم الكفر وكل ما لايليق بجنابه تعالى حتى على الصبي العاقل وروى عن ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى لا عذر لاحد في الجهل بخالقه لمايرى عن الدلائل اقول لعل المراد بعد مضى مدة التأمل فانه بمنزلة دعوة الرسل في تنبيه القلب وتلك المدة مختلفة فان العقول متفاوتة وبما حررنا من المذاهب يتفرع عليه مسألة البالغ في شاهق الجبل ترجمہ : ” پھر بعض علماء حنفیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے بعض احکام کے ادراک کرنے میں عقل مستقل ہے چنانچہ اس لئے انہوں نے (مکلف پر ) حتی کہ صبی عاقل پر ایمان کو واجب قرار دیا اور کفر کو اور ہر اس چیز کو جو جناب باری تعالیٰ کے شایان شان نہیں ہے حرام کہا ہے اور امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ سے مروی ہے کہ اپنے خالق سے جاہل رہ جانے میں کسی کا کوئی عذر مقبول نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی نگاہ میں خالق کے وجود پر دلائل قائم ہیں۔ میں سمجھتا ہوں کہ شاید غور و فکر کا زمانہ ختم ہونے کے بعد ( کوئی عذر مقبول نہ ہوگا) کیونکہ مدت تأمل قلب کو بیدار کرنے میں رسولوں کی دعوت کے منزلے میں ہے اور یہ مدت تأمل ( مختلف لوگوں کے اعتبار سے ) مختلف ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ عقلیں باہم متفاوت ہیں اور جو مذاہب ہم نے حیطہ تحریر میں لا دیا ہے اس سے شاھق جبل میں بالغ ہونے والے کا مسئلہ متفرع ہوتا ہے تشریح : گذشتہ اوراق میں بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ احناف حسن و فتح کے عقلی ہونے میں اہل اعتزال کے ساتھ متفق ہونے کے باوجود وجوب حکم کے قائل نہیں ہیں بلکہ فعل کا حسن و قبح حکم کے راجحیت کی علت ہے پس ایمان و کفر اللہ عز شانہ کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک بالکل مساوی نہیں ہو سکتے جیسا کہ بادی الرائی میں وہم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ ایسا حکیم ہے جو اپنی حکمت وارادہ کے مقتضی سے غیر مرجح کا حکم نہیں دے سکتا یا مرجوح کو ترجیح نہیں دے سکتا اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ ایمان کا وجوب رائج اور کفر کی حرمت رائج اس لئے دونوں مساوی نہیں ہو سکتے تاہم حسن و فتح حکم کو ستلزم نہیں ہیں جیسا کہ معتزلہ حکم کو لازم واجب مانتے ہیں۔ مگر بعض حنفیہ نے اپنی جماعت احناف سے اس باب میں اختلاف کیا ہے کہ بعض مواضع میں حسن وقتی مستلزم حکم ہوتا ہے تو مصنف نے ان بعض احناف کے ذکر کا ارادہ کیا جو اس مسئلہ میں جمیع احناف سے اختلاف رکھتے ہیں اس لئے کہا۔
Matn: 'Then among the Hanafis are those who said that reason may be independent in perceiving some of His rulings. Thus they obligated faith and prohibited disbelief and everything unbefitting His majesty, even upon a rational child. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): No one has any excuse for ignorance of his Creator, because he sees clear proofs.' I say: Perhaps what is meant is after the passage of a period of reflection, for it is like the invitation of messengers in awakening the heart. And that period varies, because intellects differ. And from what we have recorded of the schools, the case of the person who reaches puberty on a mountain peak branches out from it. Translation: 'Then some Hanafi scholars said that reason is independent in perceiving some of Allah's rulings. Therefore, they declared faith obligatory (even upon a rational child) and prohibited disbelief and everything unbefitting His majesty. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that no one has any excuse for ignorance of his Creator, because in his view proofs for the Creator's existence are established. I think that perhaps after the period of reflection ends (the excuse is not accepted), because the period of reflection is like the invitation of messengers in awakening the heart, and this period varies because intellects differ. And from the schools we have recorded, the case of the person who reaches puberty on a mountain peak branches out from it.' Explanation: In previous pages it was mentioned that the Hanafis, despite agreeing with the Mu'tazila that good and evil are rational, do not hold that it obligates a ruling. Rather, the act's good and evil are a cause for the preponderance of a ruling. So faith and disbelief, relative to Allah, are not equal as might be initially imagined, because He is so wise that He cannot command what is not preponderant according to His wisdom and will, nor give preference to the preponderant. It is clear that the obligation of faith and prohibition of disbelief are both established, so they cannot be equal. However, good and evil do not necessitate a ruling as the Mu'tazila hold them to be necessary and obligatory. But some Hanafis from their group differed in this chapter, saying that in some situations, good temporarily necessitates a ruling. So the author intended to mention those some Hanafis who hold this difference from the rest of the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the independence of reason in deriving rulings. The author (in the matn) notes that some Hanafis claim that reason can independently know some of Allah's rulings, such as the obligation of faith and the prohibition of disbelief, even for a rational child. This view is attributed to Abu Hanifa in a narration. The commentary (sharh) clarifies that this does not mean reason alone creates obligation; rather, after a period of reflection, and given the clear proofs in creation, ignorance becomes inexcusable. The commentary then contrasts the Hanafi majority position with the Mu'tazila: while Hanafis (like Mu'tazila) affirm that good and evil are rationally known, they do not hold that reason alone imposes a binding ruling (wujub). Instead, good and evil are causes (illat) for the preponderance of a ruling but do not necessitate it. However, a minority of Hanafis hold that in some cases, the good of an act temporarily necessitates a ruling. This minority view is the subject of the matn's mention. The passage ends by noting that this dispute branches out into the issue of a person who reaches puberty on a mountain peak (i.e., without access to revelation), which is a classic problem in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
عقل ('aql): Reason or intellect, which can perceive some rulings or their moral qualities but, according to majority Hanafis, does not independently impose obligation.
حسن و قبح (husn wa qubh): The moral categories of good and evil, which are rationally known but, per majority Hanafis, are only causes for preponderance of a ruling, not its necessity.
استلزام (istilzam): Necessitation; the idea that the goodness of an act directly entails a binding ruling. The majority Hanafis reject istilzam, while the minority accept it in some cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the majority Hanafi position regarding the role of reason in determining the obligation of faith?
A) Reason alone makes faith obligatory, even without revelation.
B) Reason knows that faith is good, but obligation comes from divine command, not reason alone.
C) Reason cannot know good or evil at all.
D) Reason and revelation are equally independent sources of obligation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a legitimate internal dispute on whether reason independently imposes any rulings; the majority holds that rational knowledge of good and evil does not create obligation, which requires divine command.

10 min
Hanafi Proof for Rational Good and Evil
Hanafi proof for rational husn/qubh with Ash'ari objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi proof for the rational nature of good and evil and respond to the Ash'ari objection using the distinction between intrinsic and relational attributes.

Core Idea
Reason alone knows kindness is good and harm is evil – proven by universal agreement, even among those who reject revelation.

This passage presents one of the most fundamental debates in usul al-fiqh: can the human intellect independently judge actions as good or evil without revelation? The Hanafi school answers yes, and here you will see their key proof, the Ash'ari objection, and the Hanafi defense. By working through this dispute, you will deepen your understanding of how the Hanafi school sources moral knowledge and where it parts from Ash'ari epistemology.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the claim (husn/qubh are intrinsic and rational) and the evidence: universal agreement of all rational people, even deniers of sharia, on the goodness of ihsan and evil of isa'ah.
Note the key phrase: 'sare arbāb-e aql o fahm... muttafiq hain'.
2
Identify the Ash'ari objection
Find the objection raised in the margin: the agreement might be about perfection/deficiency (kamāl/nuqṣān), not about deserving reward/punishment (istiḥqāq thawāb/iqāb) – the latter being the disputed sense.
The objection targets the wajh al-dalālah: does the agreement really entail the disputed meaning?
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response argues that perfection/deficiency necessarily implies praiseworthiness and blameworthiness, which is equivalent to deserving reward/punishment. Therefore, even if the agreement is about kamāl/nuqṣān, it still supports the Hanafi claim.
This response uses the principle that attributes of perfection inherently entail praise and reward.
4
Evaluate the Ash'ari counter-response (maslahah)
The Ash'aris offer an alternative explanation: the agreement is due to general benefit (maslahah 'ammah), not intrinsic qualities. The intellect rules goodness because of benefit, not essence.
This is the central point of dispute: is the moral quality intrinsic (dhati) or relational (idafi)?
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For Hanafis, some obligations (e.g., gratitude to a benefactor) are known by reason alone, so they are binding even without a revealed text. Ash'aris deny any obligation without revelation.
This affects the scope of usul: Hanafis include rational proofs (adillah aqliyyah) as a source of rulings.

تشريح - قوله لنا أن حسن الاحسان وقبح مقابلته بالاساءة الخ
یہاں سے حسن و فتح کے عقلی ہونے پر معاشر حنفیہ کی طرف سے مصنف نے دلیل قائم کی ہے۔ حاصل دلیل:۔ یہ کہ ہم معاشر حنفیہ کے نزدیک افعال کا حسن و فتح ذاتی ہے اس لئے کہ فعل احسان کے حسن ہونے پر اور احسان کی ضد اساءت کے قبیح ہونے پر سارے ہی ارباب عقل و فہم حتی کہ براہمہ و ملاحدہ اور تمام وہ لوگ جو شرع کو مطلقا نہیں مانتے متفق ہیں ۔ پس اگر حسن و فتح افعال کے لئے ذاتی وعقلی نہیں ہوتے جن کو افعال میں بالضرورة ادراک کیا جاتا ہے تو کبھی بھی سارے عقلاء کا اتفاق نہ ہوتا کیونکہ حسن و فتح اگر شرع سے ہو تا فعل سے نہ ہوتا تو منکرین شرع ہرگز احسان کے حسن کا اور اساءت کے فتح کا اقرار نہ کرتے بلکہ بلا توقف انکار کر دیتے کہ اصل (شرع) سے انکار فرع (حکم شرع) سے انکار کو ستلزم ہے۔ لہذا منکرین شرع کا احسان کے حسن پر اور اساءت کے فتح پر متفق ہونا دلیل ہے کہ احسان کا حسن اور اساءت وفتح ہے اور جب خاص فعل احسان و اساعت میں حسن و فتح کا ذاتی و عقلی ہونا ثابت ہو گیا ذاتی و عقلی ہونا ثابت ہو گیا تو جملہ افعال میں حسن و فتح کو عقلی وذاتی ماننا ہوگا اسلئے کہ ہمارا، معتزلہ اور اشاعرہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ حسن و فتح عقلی وذاتی ہے تو سب میں ہے اور شرعی ہے تو سب میں ۔ قول بالفصل کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے۔
اشکال - دلیل مذکور پر ایک قومی اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے جسکو ماتن نے حاشیہ میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ لك أن تقول أن اتفاقهم على ذالك يجوز أن يكون لانهما من صفات الكمال والنقصان كوجوب الصدق وامتناع الكذب فى حقه تعالى واما بالمغى المتنازع فيه فربما يمنع انتهت
یعنی فعل احسان کے حسن ہونے پر اور اس کی ضد اساءت کے قبیح ہونے پر اگر چہ تمام عقلاء کے اتفاق کو ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں لیکن ہم یہ تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ عقلاء کا یہ اتفاق حسن و قبیح کے معنی متنازع فیہ یعنی استحقاق ثواب و عقاب میں ہے یہاں تک کہ حسن و فتح کو فعل کے لئے ذاتی ہونا ثابت کیا جائے اور یہ کہا جائے کہ عقل بذاتہ بغیر استعانت شرع دونوں فعل کا حسن و فتح ادراک کر لیتی ہے! ایسا کیوں نہیں ممکن ہے کہ احسان کے حسن اور اساءت کے فتح پر عقلاء کے مابین جوا تفاق ہے وہ صفت کمال و نقصان کے معنی میں ہو جس کے عقلی ہونے پر پہلے ہی اتفاق ہو چکا ہے۔ غرض عقلاء کا یہ اتفاق آپ کے لئے فائدہ مند نہیں جس کے آپ ثابت کرنے کے درپے ہیں۔
جواب:۔ بعض محققین نے درج بالا اعتراض کا یوں جواب دیا ہے کہ معترض کو جب یہ تسلیم ہے کہ حسن وقیح کے معنی صفت کمال و صفت نقصان پر عقلاء کا اتفاق ہے تو گویا اس کو یہ تسلیم ہے کہ حسن و فتح کے معنی استحقاق مدح و ذم و استحقاق ثواب و عقاب پر عقلاء کا اتفاق ہے، کیونکہ صفت کمال و نقصان ممدوحیت دند مومیت، واستحقاق مدروحیت و ندمومیت یا استحقاق عقاب و ثواب کے مغائر نہیں ہے بلکہ صفت کمال و نقصان، ممدوحیث و مذمومیت یا استحقاق ثواب و عقاب ہر ایک کا مفاد و مصداق یکساں ہے لہذا حسن و فتح کا معنی صفت کمال نقصان مراد لیں خواہ استحقاق ثواب کے معنی میں لیں بہر دوصورت مطلوب ثابت ہوگا اسطور پر کہ ممدوحیت و مذمومیت اگر نظر شارع میں ہے تو کوئی شبہ نہیں کہ یہ معنی متنازع فیہ استحقاق ثواب و عقاب کی طرف راجع ہو گا اس صورت میں منع وارد کرنا از قبیل مکابرہ ہوگا اگر مد وحیت وندمومیت نظر غیر شارع میں ہے تو پوچھا جائے گا کہ نظر غیر شارع میں ممدوح و مذموم ہونے کا کیا مطلب ہے؟ اگر غیر شارع کی نظر میں ممدوح و مذموم ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ غیر شارع ممدوح کو مستحق ثواب اور مذموم کو مستحق عقاب سمجھتا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی معترض کو کوئی فائدہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس کے لئے مضر ہوگا۔
قوله والجواب بانه يجوزان يكون لمصلحة عامة.
اس عبارت سے حنفیہ کی دلیل مذکور کا جواب اشاعرہ کی طرف سے ہے، اشاعرہ کہتے ہیں کہ احسان کے حسن اور اساءت کے فتح پر عقلاء کے اتفاق کو ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں لیکن یہ نہیں تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ عقلاء کا یہ اتفاق حسن و قبح کے ذاتی و عقلی ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے بلکہ احسان میں چونکہ جمیع خلائق کے لئے مصلحت عامہ وابستہ ہے اس لئے عقل نے رعایت مفاد عامہ کے پیش نظر احسان میں حسن ہونے کا حکم لگا دیا اور اساءت میں چونکہ مصلحت عامہ کا نقص و مفسدہ ہے اس لئے عقل نے اس کے قبیح ہونے کا حکم لگایا بہر حال احسان و اساءت کا حسن و فتح ذات فعل کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ مصلحت عامہ کی رعایت و عدم رعایت کی وجہ سے ہے۔
Commentary - His statement 'for us that the goodness of ihsan and the evil of reciprocating with isa'ah, etc.' From here, the author presents a proof on behalf of the Hanafi school that good and evil are rational. Summary of the proof: We, the Hanafi school, hold that good and evil are intrinsic to actions because all people of intellect and understanding, even the Brahmins and heretics and all those who do not believe in sharia at all, agree that the act of ihsan is good and its opposite isa'ah is evil. So if good and evil were not intrinsic and rational, perceived necessarily in actions, then all rational people would never have agreed, because if good and evil came from sharia and not from the action, then the deniers of sharia would never affirm the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah, but would immediately deny it, because denial of the principle (sharia) necessitates denial of the branch (sharia ruling). Therefore, the agreement of the deniers of sharia on the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah is proof that the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah exist and are intrinsic and rational. And when it is established that good and evil are intrinsic and rational in the specific actions of ihsan and isa'ah, then it is necessary to hold that good and evil in all actions are rational and intrinsic, because there is agreement between us, the Mu'tazila, and the Ash'aris that if good and evil are rational and intrinsic, they are in all actions, and if they are sharia-based, they are in all actions. There is no one who differentiates. Objection - Some people raise an objection to the mentioned proof, which the author mentioned in the commentary. 'You may say that their agreement on that may be because these two are attributes of perfection and deficiency, like the obligation of truthfulness and the impossibility of lying with respect to Allah, and as for the meaning under dispute, perhaps it is prevented.' That is, regarding the goodness of ihsan and the evil of its opposite isa'ah, although we accept the agreement of all rational people, we do not accept that this agreement is in the disputed sense of good and evil, i.e., deserving reward and punishment, so that good and evil are proven to be intrinsic to the action and it is said that the intellect by itself perceives the good and evil of both actions without the aid of sharia! Why is it not possible that the agreement among rational people on the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah is in the sense of attributes of perfection and deficiency, the rationality of which has already been agreed upon? In short, this agreement of the rational people is not beneficial for you to prove what you are aiming to prove. Response - Some scholars have responded to the above objection as follows: When the objector concedes that there is agreement among rational people on good and evil in the sense of attributes of perfection and deficiency, then he has effectively conceded that there is agreement among rational people on good and evil in the sense of deserving praise and blame and deserving reward and punishment, because attributes of perfection and deficiency are not different from praiseworthiness and blameworthiness and deserving reward and punishment. Rather, the meaning and referent of attributes of perfection and deficiency and praiseworthiness and blameworthiness or deserving reward and punishment are all the same. Therefore, whether good and evil are taken to mean attributes of perfection and deficiency or in the sense of deserving reward, in both cases the desired conclusion is proven. In other words, if praiseworthiness and blameworthiness are from the perspective of the Lawgiver, then there is no doubt that this meaning reverts to the disputed meaning of deserving reward and punishment, so in that case raising an objection would be mere obstinacy. If praiseworthiness and blameworthiness are from the perspective of other than the Lawgiver, then it will be asked: what is the meaning of being praiseworthy and blameworthy in the view of other than the Lawgiver? If the meaning in the view of other than the Lawgiver is that the praiseworthy is deserving of reward and the blameworthy is deserving of punishment, then even in this case the objector derives no benefit; rather, it is harmful for him. His statement 'and the response is that it is possible that it is for a general interest.' This phrase is the response of the Ash'aris to the mentioned Hanafi proof. The Ash'aris say: We accept the agreement of rational people on the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah, but we do not accept that this agreement is due to their being intrinsic and rational good and evil. Rather, because in ihsan there is a general interest for all creatures, the intellect has ruled that it is good out of consideration for the common good. And because in isa'ah there is harm and corruption of the general interest, the intellect has ruled that it is evil. In any case, the goodness of ihsan and the evil of isa'ah are not due to the essence of the action, but rather due to the observance or non-observance of the general interest.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute on the nature of good (husn) and evil (qubh) of actions. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi proof that good and evil are intrinsic (dhati) and rational (aqli) attributes. The proof rests on the universal agreement of all rational people, including atheists and heretics, that kindness (ihsan) is good and its opposite, harm (isa'ah), is evil. The argument is that if these judgments depended on revelation, those who reject revelation would not agree. The fact that they do agree shows the intellect can independently recognize good and evil. An objection is then raised: perhaps the agreement is only about perfection and deficiency, not about deserving reward and punishment, which is the real point of contention. A Hanafi response follows, arguing that perfection/deficiency and deserving reward/punishment are essentially the same—both relate to praiseworthiness and blameworthiness. Finally, the Ash'ari position is presented: they accept the agreement but attribute it to general benefit (maslahah 'ammah) rather than intrinsic qualities. The commentary follows the author's order: proof, objection, response, and counter-position. Throughout, the Hanafi view is that the intellect is a valid source of moral knowledge, while the Ash'aris limit moral knowledge to revelation.

Key Terms
حسن (husn): Goodness of an action; in this dispute, either intrinsic and perceived by reason, or determined by revelation.
قبح (qubh): Evil of an action; similar to husn, subject to the same dispute.
ذاتی (dhati): Intrinsic; belonging to the essence of the action, not derived from external factors.
عقلی (aqli): Rational; knowable by reason independently of revelation.
مصلحت عامہ (maslahah 'ammah): General benefit or public interest; the Ash'ari explanation for why rational people agree on goodness of ihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi proof in this passage, why does the universal agreement of all rational people (including atheists) on the goodness of kindness and evil of harm prove that these moral judgments are intrinsic and rational?
A) Because atheists would not agree if the judgment were based on revelation, showing the judgment must come from reason alone.
B) Because the Quran commands kindness and prohibits harm, and atheists accidentally follow the Quran.
C) Because Abu Hanifa declared that rational agreement is equivalent to revelation.
D) Because the agreement is actually about social benefit, not intrinsic qualities.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi proof for rational husn and qubh relies on universal agreement, which shows that moral judgments can be independent of revelation, though revelation remains the primary source for detailed rulings.

Essential Evil and Accidental Good Are Compatible
Explains compatibility of essential evil and accidental good

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that essential evil (qabīḥ li-dhātihī) and accidental good (ḥasan li-ghayrihī) can coexist in a single act, and distinguish between the two aspects (essence vs. attribute) to resolve apparent moral contradictions.

Core Idea
An act can be inherently evil yet good due to an external factor — no contradiction because the aspects differ.

This passage clarifies a key Hanafi usul principle: moral attributes like good and evil can attach to different aspects of the same act. Lying is inherently evil, but if it saves a prophet, it becomes good due to that external purpose. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion when rulings seem contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its attributes
The act under discussion is lying (kadhib). The text assigns it two attributes: essential evil (qabīḥ li-dhātihī) and accidental good (ḥasan li-ghayrihī) due to saving a prophet.
The inherent evil never changes; the goodness is contingent on an external factor.
2
Understand the objection and response
An objector (Mirza Jan) argues that an act cannot be both good and evil. The Hanafi response says this is only impossible if considered from one aspect; here the aspects differ (essence vs. attribute).
The objection assumes a single aspect, which is not the case.
3
Distinguish essence from attribute
The text clarifies that evil and prohibition are attached to the essence (dhāt) of an act, while goodness and obligation are attached to an external attribute (ṣifah) adjacent to the act, such as saving a life.
Thus the ruling varies based on which aspect is considered.
4
Connect to the maxim of necessity
The author supports his answer by citing the legal maxim 'Necessities permit prohibitions' (al-ḍarūrāt tubīḥ al-maḥẓūrāt), using the example of carrion: it remains inherently forbidden but becomes permissible under dire hunger due to necessity.
The permissibility is accidental, not essential.
5
Formulate the general rule
Essential evil and accidental good are compatible because they attach to different loci (essence vs. attribute). The combination of opposites requires a single aspect; with multiple aspects, there is no contradiction.
This is a foundational principle for deriving rulings in cases of conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اقول الحسن لغيره لاينافى القبيح لذاته وهذا
اس عبارت سے فاضل مرزا جان کے اشکال کا جواب دیا ہے۔
جواب: - کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم کو یہ تسلیم ہے کہ یہاں کذب واجب ہے اور یہ بھی تسلیم ہے کہ وجوب، کذب کے حسن کا متقضی ہے لیکن اس کے باوجود پھر بھی کذب قبیح کا حسن ہونا یا حرام کا واجب ہونا نہیں لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ فتح وحرمت نظر کرتے ہوئے ذات کذب کی طرف ہے اور وجوب وحسن نظر کرتے ہوئے اس وصف کی طرف ہے جو کذب سے مجاور ہے اور وہ وصف نبی و بری کو ظالم و قاتل سے بچانا ہے۔ چنانچہ یہ محال نہیں کہ کذب نفس ذات کے اعتبار فتح ہومگر وصف کے اعتبار سے حسن ہو محال یہ ہے کہ شئی ذات ہی کے اعتبار قبیح حسن یا واجب و حرام دونوں ہو۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ کذب کا فتح ذاتی ہے اور حسن عرضی ہے اور فتح لذاتہ، حسن لغیرہ کے منافی نہیں ہے
دونوں کا اجتماع ہوسکتا ہے۔
قوله وهذا معنى قولهم الضرورات تبيح المحظورات مصنف نے اس عبارت سے اپنے جواب کی تائید میں فقہاء کے قول سے استناد کیا ہے کہتے ہیں کہ فقہاء کے ارشاد الضرورات تیج المطورات کا یہی مطلب ہے کہ بر بنائے ضرورت محرمات وممنوعات کے ساتھ مباح جیسا معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے اس کا یہ معنی نہیں ہے کہ وہ ممنوعات باعتبار ذات مباح ہو جاتی ہیں بلکہ باعتبار ذات وہ افعال ممنوعہ محرم ہی رہتی ہیں البتہ باعتبار غیر یعنی ضرورت و حرج وغیرہ مباح کہلاتی ہیں جیسے مخمصہ کہ وہ میتہ کو بر بنائے ضرورت ہی بقدر ضرورت مباح کرتی ہے باوجود یکہ میتہ محرمہ ہے۔ غرض میتہ کی حرمت ذاتیہ ہے اور اباحت غیر یہ ہے اور اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ۔ قوله - غاية الامرانه يلزم القول بأن كلا منهما الخ اس عبارت سے کہنا چاہتے ہیں کہ فاضل معترض کی اگر یہ مراد ہے کہ شی واحد کا جہت واحدہ سے حسن و قبیح ہونا اور حرام و واجب ہونا لازم آئے گا تو یہ منوع ہے اور اگر یہ مراد ہے کہ شئی واحد کا با عتبار جہتیں حسن و قبیح ہونا اور حرام و واجب ہونالازم آئے گا تو یہ مسلم ہے لیکن استحالہ غیر مسلم ہے کیونکہ اجتماع متنافیین کے لئے محل واحد کے ساتھ جہت واحدہ ضروری ہے اور یہاں جہت واحدہ نہیں ہے بلکہ تعدد جہات ہے باعتبار ذات فتح ہے اور باعتبار وصف وعرض حسن ہے گویا حسن و فتح کا تعلق بالاعتبا ۔ دو محل کے ساتھ ہے۔
He said: I say that good due to another does not contradict evil in itself. And this is the answer to the objection of the virtuous Mirza Jan. The summary of the answer is that we concede that lying here is obligatory, and we also concede that obligation necessitates the goodness of lying, but despite that, it does not require that the evil becomes good or the forbidden becomes obligatory, because considered from the perspective of evil and prohibition, it is directed to the essence of lying, and considered from the perspective of obligation and goodness, it is directed to the attribute adjacent to lying, which is saving the prophet and innocent from the oppressor and killer. Thus, it is not impossible for lying to be evil in its essence but good in terms of attribute; what is impossible is for a thing to be both evil and good or obligatory and forbidden in its essence. In summary, lying has essential evil and accidental goodness, and essential evil does not contradict accidental goodness; both can coexist. He said: And this is the meaning of their statement: Necessities permit prohibitions. The author used this statement from the jurists to support his answer. He says that the meaning of the jurists' saying 'Necessities permit prohibitions' is that due to necessity, prohibited things are treated as permissible; it does not mean that those prohibitions become permissible in essence, rather in essence those prohibited acts remain forbidden, but due to another factor, i.e., necessity and hardship, they are called permissible, like the case of dire hunger that permits carrion only to the extent of necessity, even though carrion is forbidden. In short, carrion has essential prohibition and accidental permissibility, and there is no harm in that. He said: The ultimate point is that it necessitates saying that each of them... From this phrase, he intends to say that if the objecting scholar means that a single thing from one aspect is both good and evil, and forbidden and obligatory, then this is denied; and if he means that a single thing from multiple aspects is both good and evil, and forbidden and obligatory, then this is accepted, but the impossibility is not accepted, because for the combination of opposites, a single locus with a single aspect is necessary, and here there is not a single aspect but multiple aspects: in terms of essence it is evil, and in terms of attribute and accident it is good. So goodness and evil are attached to two different loci.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the compatibility of essential evil and accidental good. The commentator addresses an objection by Mirza Jan regarding lying being obligatory. The author admits lying is inherently evil (قبیح لذاتہ) but good due to saving a prophet (حسن لغیرہ). He explains that the evil is attached to the essence of lying, while the goodness is attached to the external attribute (saving someone). Thus, one act can have both qualities without contradiction. He supports this by citing the legal maxim 'Necessities permit prohibitions', giving the example of carrion (میتہ) which is inherently forbidden but becomes permissible under necessity. The permissibility is accidental, not essential. He then clarifies that if an objector says a single thing from one aspect cannot be both good and evil, that is correct; but if from multiple aspects, it is possible. This is because opposites require a single aspect and locus; here the aspects differ (essence vs. attribute). The commentary follows the order of the original text, first stating the principle, then supporting it with fiqh examples, and finally refining the logical point about multiple aspects.

Key Terms
قبیح لذاتہ (qabīḥ li-dhātihī): Evil in itself, an inherent attribute of an act that never changes.
حسن لغیرہ (ḥasan li-ghayrihī): Good due to another, an accidental attribute acquired from an external factor.
الضرورات تبیح المحظورات (al-ḍarūrāt tubīḥu al-maḥẓūrāt): A legal maxim meaning necessities make forbidden things permissible, but only to the extent needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Essential evil and accidental good can coexist in one act because they apply to different aspects.

Five Types of Good and Evil by Rational Probability
Classification of good and evil into five types based on rational probability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the five rational classifications of good and evil, distinguish between essential and accidental evil, and apply these distinctions to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Evil in itself is the absence of perfection; what leads to evil is evil by accident, not in essence.

This passage presents a nuanced classification of good and evil based on rational probability, a key concept in Hanafi-Maturidi usul al-fiqh. It addresses the theological problem of evil by distinguishing between intrinsic evil (sharr bi al-dhat) and accidental evil (sharr bi al-'arad). Understanding this classification is essential for grasping how divine wisdom permits apparent evils for greater goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
The passage argues that something leading to evil (like cold spoiling fruit) is not evil in itself; only the absence of perfection is evil. This distinguishes intrinsic from accidental evil.
Focus on the example of coldness and the quote from Tusi.
2
Analyze the example of jihad
Jihad involves destruction but leads to abundant good (elevation of Allah's word). Therefore, the destruction is sharr bi al-'arad, not sharr bi al-dhat.
This illustrates how means are judged by their ends.
3
Memorize the five categories
The five types are: (1) pure good (khayr mahd), (2) pure evil (sharr mahd), (3) equal good and evil, (4) good predominant (khayr ghalib), (5) evil predominant (sharr ghalib). Only (1) and (4) exist in reality.
Pure good is unique to Allah; pure evil, equal, and evil predominant do not exist.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a scenario (e.g., a bitter medicine that cures illness), classify the bad taste as sharr bi al-'arad and explain why it is not evil in itself.
Practice using the categories to analyze everyday cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مظلوم کی طرف، سیاست مدینہ کی طرف اور اس نفس ناطقہ کی طرف جو دونوں قوت حیوانیہ کی ضبط کے متحمل نہیں ہیں۔ الغرض شر بالذات ان اشیاء میں سے کسی ایک کے کمال کا فقدان ہے رہے اس کے اسباب پر جو شر کا اطلاق کیا جاتا ہے وہ شر بالعرض ہے کہ وہ ان اشیاء کی ہلاکت کی طرف مودی ہوتا ہے انتھی“ اس تقریر سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ مفضی الی الشر بالذات شر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ شر بالعرض ہوتا ہے ... اسی طرح مفضی الی الخیر کا بالذات اس حیثیت سے خیر ہونا بھی ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ خیر بالعرض ہوتا ہے نہیں بلکہ مفضی الی الخیر بھی کبھی شر ہو سکتا ہے۔ فائدہ:۔ احتمالات عقلیہ کے اعتبار سے خیر وشر کی کل پانچ قسمیں ہیں ۔ (۱) خیر محض ۔ (۲) شرمحض ۔ (۳) خیر وشر مساوی ۔ (۴) خیر غالب شرمغلوب۔ (۵) شر غالب خیر مغلوب۔ (۱) خیر محض وہ ہے جو عدم کو نہ قبول کرے اس لئے کہ عدم شر محض ہوتا ہے یہ قسم واجب تعالیٰ کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ (۲) خیر غالب شر مغلوب جیسے ملائکہ و انبیاء کا وجود و بعثت، چنانچہ ان دونوں ذوات قدسیہ میں عدم سابق و عدم لاحق کے ماسواء شر اقل قلیل ہے کہ حضرات ملائکہ حکم الہی سے انبیاء کی تائید فرماتے ہیں اور ایسے احکام لیکر آئے ہیں جن میں شر قلیل پایا جاتا ہے جیسے جہاد کہ اس سے کفار و مشرکین کی ہلاکت ہوتی ہے غرض ملائکہ کا وجود اور انبیاء کی بعثت خیر محض نہیں جیسا کہ بعض شراح کو وہم ہوا۔ خیر وشر کی بقیہ تینوں قسمیں (۳) خیر و شر مساوی (۴) شر محض - (۵) شر غالب اور خیر مغلوب موجود نہیں ہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اللہ علیم وخبیر کا مقصود تخلیق عالم اور اس کا حسن انتظام ہے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ اس میں خیر شر پر غالب ہے گو کہ بعض آحاد میں شر خیر پر غالب ہو یا مساوی ہو۔ هذا ما قاله الفاضل خیر آبادی علیه الرحمه
Leaving abundant good is far from the dignity of the Wise, so evil was apportioned and given existence. For example, consider jihad: Allah made it obligatory upon the Prophet and his Muslim nation, even though it involves the destruction of disbelievers and their ruin, but it contains abundant good that far outweighs the destruction of disbelievers — it is the elevation of Allah's word, the implementation of Shari'ah rulings that contain worldly and otherworldly benefit, the illumination of the light of truth and the lamp of faith, and the extinguishing of the darkness of disbelief and transgression, etc. That which leads to evil in itself is not evil. Further elaboration by Tusi in Sharh al-Isharat: For example, coldness that spoils fruits is not evil in itself, neither as a quality nor as an efficient cause; rather, it is evil only by analogy to fruits because it corrupts their temperaments. Likewise, oppression and adultery, insofar as they emanate from the powers of anger and lust, are not evil; rather, they manifest the perfection of those powers. But they are evil from the perspective of the oppressed, the civil polity, and the rational soul that cannot bear the control of these animal powers. In short, evil in itself is the absence of perfection in something; the application of evil to its causes is evil by accident, because they lead to the destruction of those things. End quote. From this discourse, it is understood that what leads to evil in itself is not evil but rather evil by accident. Similarly, what leads to good in itself is not necessarily good; rather, it is good by accident. Indeed, what leads to good can sometimes be evil. Benefit: According to rational probability, good and evil are of five types: (1) Pure good; (2) Pure evil; (3) Equal good and evil; (4) Good predominant, evil subjugated; (5) Evil predominant, good subjugated. (1) Pure good: that which does not accept non-existence because non-existence is pure evil. This type is specific to the Necessary Being. (2) Good predominant, evil subjugated: like the existence and missions of angels and prophets. In these two sacred beings, besides prior and posterior non-existence, there is minimal evil. Angels, by divine command, support prophets and bring rulings in which little evil is found, such as jihad which causes the destruction of disbelievers. Thus the existence of angels and the missions of prophets are not pure good, as some commentators mistakenly thought. The remaining three types — (3) equal good and evil, (4) pure evil, (5) evil predominant and good subjugated — do not exist. The summary is that Allah, the All-Knowing and All-Aware, intends the creation of the universe and its beautiful order, and there is no doubt that good prevails over evil, even if in some individuals evil may prevail over good or be equal. This is what al-Fadil Khayrabadi said, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the nature of good and evil, particularly regarding divine actions and the problem of evil. The author first argues that God's wisdom involves permitting evil because it leads to greater good, using jihad as an example where destruction of disbelievers is outweighed by the benefit of establishing Islam. He then elaborates on the concept that something leading to evil is not evil in itself, citing Tusi's example of coldness spoiling fruits: coldness is not evil per se but becomes evil by association with its effect. Similarly, oppression and adultery are not evil when considered as manifestations of natural powers, but are evil from the perspective of the victim and society. Thus, evil in itself is defined as the absence of perfection in a thing. The passage then classifies good and evil into five possible types based on rational probability: pure good (only for Allah), pure evil (non-existent), equal good and evil (non-existent), good predominant over evil (e.g., angels and prophets), and evil predominant over good (non-existent). The author emphasizes that in the actual world, good predominates, and even in cases where evil seems equal or dominant, the overall cosmic order is good. This is a common Ash'ari/Maturidi theme, but here it is presented in a Hanafi usul context as part of the discussion on the wisdom of divine actions.

Key Terms
خیر بالذات (khayr bi al-dhat): Good in itself, inherent goodness independent of consequences.
شر بالذات (sharr bi al-dhat): Evil in itself, inherent badness defined as absence of perfection in a thing.
شر بالعرض (sharr bi al-'arad): Evil by accident, i.e., something that leads to evil but is not evil in itself.
خیر غالب (khayr ghalib): Good predominant over evil; the only type existing in creation besides pure good.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many of the five types of good and evil actually exist in reality?
A) Five
B) Two
C) Three
D) One

Key Takeaway
In the actual creation, only pure good (Allah) and good predominant over evil exist; all other rational possibilities are non-existent.

Author's Justification for Including the Free Will Discussion
Commentary explaining the rationale for including a free will discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author inserted the free will discussion as a 'fā'ida' and identify the ordering methodology used in presenting different legal schools.

Core Idea
False schools are refuted first so that the truth is more impactful when presented last.

This short commentary clarifies that the discussion on free will (jabr wa ikhtiyār) is not a random digression. It was prompted by the Ash'ari's third argument regarding the Shar'i nature of good and evil, which rested on the issue of human capacity. The commentator then reveals the author's deliberate method: he lists four schools, explicitly rejects the first two (Jahmiyya and Mu'tazila), marks the third (Ash'ariyya) as also not preferred, and finally states the fourth (Hanafī) as the truth, so that after refuting falsehood, the truth has a stronger effect on the soul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reason for inclusion
The commentator states that the Ash'ari's third argument on the Shar'i nature of good/evil was based on the issue of compulsion (jabr) and choice (ikhtiyār). Therefore, the author included this discussion to address that foundation.
This shows how usul discussions often build on interrelated issues.
2
Recognize the author's classification of four schools
The author mentions four schools among the 'causes' (asbāb). The first two (Jahmiyya, then presumably Mu'tazila) are said to be clearly false. The third (Ash'ariyya) is not preferred by the author. Only the fourth (Hanafī) is considered the true position.
The classification is hierarchical, not neutral.
3
Understand the ordering principle
The commentator explicitly says: 'He mentioned the true school last, so that after refuting falsehood, establishing the truth is more impactful on the soul.' This is a pedagogical principle: clear the ground before planting the truth.
This reflects a method of al-munāẓara (scholarly debate) used in usul texts.
4
Identify the methodology used in describing the Jahmiyya school
The commentator begins describing the first school (Jahmiyya), noting their belief that the servant has absolutely no power over actions, and that they rely on the apparent meanings of Quranic verses affirming Allah as Creator of all acts.
The passage cuts off before the verse is quoted; this incomplete citation requires caution.
5
Note the incomplete nature of the passage
The source text ends mid-sentence with 'such as the verse 'And Allah...''. The full argument and Hanafi response are not provided in this chunk. This is a reminder that this is a fragment needing context.
In scholarly study, always check the full text before drawing conclusions.

قوله - عند الجهميه الذين هم الجبرية حقاً
مذہب اول : جہمیہ کا ہے یہ فرقہ جہم بن صفوان معتزلی کی طرف منسوب ہے اس لئے جہمیہ کہلاتا ہے مگر عقائد ونظریات کے اعتبار سے بالکل جبریہ کے ہم خیال ہے جبر یہ جہمیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ بندہ کو فل کے ایجاد و کسب میں مطلقا کسی قسم کی قدرت نہیں ہے بندہ اس جہاد کی طرح مجبور محض ہے جس کو کسی چیز کی مطلقا قدرت نہیں ہوتی۔ غالباً ان حمقاء نے یہ قول ان آیات مبارکہ کے ظواہر پر نظر کرتے ہوئے کیا ہے جن میں ہے کہ اللہ عز شانہ تمام افعال و اعمال کا خالق ہے جیسے آیت والله
Elucidation: His saying 'a benefit' – you will recall that the Ash'ari's third argument on the Shari'i nature of beauty and ugliness was based on the issue of compulsion and choice. Therefore, the author mentioned here the issue of determinism and free will as a benefit. Since the issue of determinism and free will is one of the most important issues of the fundamentals of religion, in which the feet of great intelligent scholars have stumbled and the minds of great people of intellect have become bewildered in this path, therefore the author said 'a benefit.'
The issue of determinism and free will is a highly debated topic. The author (matn) has mentioned four considered schools among the causes. Among them, the first two schools are clearly false, and the third and fourth are of the people of truth. But the third school is also disliked by the author; only the fourth or last school is true according to him. Therefore, he mentioned the true school last, so that after refuting falsehood, establishing the truth is more impactful on the soul.
His saying: 'According to the Jahmiyya, who are truly the Jabriyya.' The first school is that of the Jahmiyya. This sect is attributed to Jahm bin Safwan al-Mu'tazili, hence called Jahmiyya, but in terms of beliefs and doctrines they are completely in agreement with the Jabriyya. The belief of the Jahmiyya is that the servant has absolutely no power of any kind in the creation and acquisition of the act; the servant is purely compelled like an inanimate object that has absolutely no power over anything. Probably these foolish people have said this based on the apparent meanings of the blessed verses in which it is stated that Allah, Exalted is His Glory, is the Creator of all acts and deeds, such as the verse 'And Allah...'

Commentary
This 'تشریح' is an explanatory note by the commentator, clarifying why the author included the discussion on determinism and free will (جبر و اختیار) as a 'benefit' (فائدة). He states that the Ash'ari argument regarding the Shari'i nature of good and evil was based on this issue, so the author brings it as an important aside. The commentator then explains the author's methodology: he lists four schools, considers the first two (Jahmiyya and Mu'tazila) clearly false, the third (Ash'ariyya) also not preferred, and the fourth (Hanafiyya) as the truth. The ordering is intentional: falsehoods are refuted first, then truth is established to have a stronger impact. Then he begins detailing the first school, Jahmiyya, explaining their belief that the servant has no power, which they derive from the apparent meaning of Quranic verses affirming Allah as Creator of all actions. The passage cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
فائدہ (fā'ida): A benefit or additional useful discussion inserted at this point in the commentary.
فرقہ جہمیہ (firqa jahmiyya): Followers of Jahm bin Safwan; they hold extreme determinism, denying human power entirely.
جبر و اختیار (jabr wa ikhtiyār): Determinism and free will; the debate on human capacity in relation to divine omnipotence.

The Hanafi Rejection of Extreme Determinism as Sophistry (Safsata)
Rational refutation of Jabriyya using badahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why Hanafi usul considers the Jabriyya view sophistry because it violates badahah, and explain how this affects the foundation of taklif (religious obligation).

Core Idea
Denying human power is sophistry — it contradicts self-evident knowledge and destroys the basis of Islamic obligation.

In this passage, the commentator refutes the extreme determinist (Jabriyya) doctrine by labeling it 'safsata' (sophistry). Rather than offering a detailed proof, he argues that the view is so obviously false — it contradicts basic human intuition (badahah) — that no elaborate refutation is needed. This illustrates a key usul principle: self-evident knowledge (badahah) can serve as a decisive arbitrator in theological and legal debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim Being Refuted
Recognize that the Jabriyya argue that humans have no effective power in their actions, based on a misinterpretation of verses like 'Khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun'.
This extreme view leads to determinism (jabr).
2
Understand the Term 'Safsata' (Sophistry)
Examine the etymology: from Greek 'sophistes' meaning false wisdom. The author uses it to dismiss the argument as fallacious and unworthy of serious debate.
In Hanafi usul, labeling an argument as 'safsata' indicates it contradicts badahah.
3
Recognize the Role of Badahah (Self-Evident Knowledge)
Identify that the author appeals to what every rational person knows intuitively: that they have power and choice in actions like eating and drinking. This is a source of certainty in Hanafi usul.
Badahah is a valid epistemological tool, especially in rational proofs (dalil aqli).
4
Trace the Consequence for Taklif
If humans had no power, then religious commands and prohibitions would be impossible (taklif bi ma la yutaq). Moreover, attributing sin directly to Allah would imply injustice, which is impossible.
This shows why the Jabriyya view is not just wrong but destructive to the entire Shariah.
5
Summarize the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school affirms that humans have an acquired power (kasb) created by Allah, which makes them responsible for their actions without attributing full creation to them.
This middle path avoids both Jabriyya and Qadariyya extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلقكم وما تعملون وغیرہ اس لئے ان کو وہم ہو گیا کہ افعال میں بندہ کی قدرت کو دخل نہیں۔ قوله وهذا سفسطة ۔ اس کا قول سفسطہ دونوں سین کے فتحہ کے ساتھ مصدر رباعی کے وزن پر ہے اور سوفسطاسے معرب ہو کر مشتق ہوا ہے اور سوفسطا، سین کے ضمہ کے ساتھ اورف کے فتحہ کے ساتھ آیا ہے جو یونانی زبان کا ایک لفظ ہے علم الغلط ، حکمت باطلہ وغیرہ معانی میں آتا ہے چونکہ سوف یونانی لغت میں علم وحکمت کو کہتے ہیں اور اسطا" کا معنی زخرف ، غلط اور باطل وغیرہ آتا ہے جس طرح فلسفہ، فیلسوف سے مشتق ہے محب الحکمۃ کو کہتے ہیں شرح مواقف میں ہے کہ فیلا یونانی لغت میں محب کو کہتے ہیں اور سوف علم کا نام ہے۔ یہ مذہب جبر چونکہ بداہتہ باطل ہے اس لئے مصنف نے اس کے رد میں کوئی دلیل ذکر کئے بغیر ہذا سفسطہ کہکر اشارہ کر دیا ہے کہ یہ مذہب لا یعبا بہ کے مرتبہ میں ہے چنانچہ ہر ذی فہم اور اہل عقل اپنی عقل و وجدان سے اتنی سی بات بداہتہ جانتا ہے اور سمجھتا ہے کہ بندہ کو ایک قسم کی قدرت حاصل ہے جس سے اس کے افعال کھانا پینا وغیرہ سرزد ہوتے ہیں اور ان افعال کا صدور بندہ سے ہواؤں کے چلنے کی طرح اور پتھر کے لڑھکنے کی طرح نہیں ہوتا بلکہ آدمی کے شعور و ادراک اور ارادہ و اختیار سے صادر ہوتے ہیں۔ ہواؤں کے چلنے اور پتھر لڑھکنے جیسے افعال کو افعال عباد کے مماثل قرار دینا بداہت کے بالمقابل مکابرہ ہے اس لئے ان کی بات غیر مسموع ہے فی الواقع اگر ایسا ہو تو تکالیف شرعیہ کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا کیونکہ عقل حاکم ہے کہ جو چیز فاعل کے لئے واجب و ممتنع ہو اس سے تکلیف کا تعلق ممتنع ہے ورنہ باری عزاسمہ کی طرف ظلم کا استناد لازم آئے گا
تعالى الله عما يقولون الظالمون علواً كبيراً
"He created you and what you do" etc. Because of this, they were deluded into thinking that the servant's power has no entry in [his] actions. His statement: "And this is sophistry." This word 'safsata' is on the pattern of a quadriliteral verbal noun with fatha on both sins, and is derived as an Arabization of 'sophistes', and 'sophista' comes with dammah on the sin and fatha on the fa', which is a Greek word meaning the science of error, false philosophy, etc. Since 'soph' in Greek means knowledge and wisdom, and 'ista' means ornament, error, falsehood, etc., just as 'falsafa' is derived from 'philosophos' meaning lover of wisdom. In Sharh al-Mawaqif it is said that 'philo' in Greek means lover and 'soph' is the name of knowledge. The madhhab of jabr (determinism), since it is obviously false, the author, without citing any proof in its refutation, indicated by saying 'this is sophistry' that this madhhab is at the level of being disregarded. Thus every intelligent and rational person knows and understands by their intellect and intuition this much as a matter of course: that the servant has a kind of power by which his actions like eating and drinking occur, and the occurrence of these actions from the servant is not like the blowing of winds or the rolling of a stone, but rather they issue from the person's consciousness, perception, intention, and choice. To equate actions like the blowing of wind and the rolling of a stone with the actions of servants is stubbornness against the obvious; therefore their statement is inadmissible. In reality, if this were the case, the door of religious obligations (taklif) would be closed, because reason rules that it is impossible for obligation to be attached to something that is necessary or impossible for the agent; otherwise, attributing injustice to Allah would be necessary. Allah is exalted above what the wrongdoers say, a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (hukm) rejecting the extreme determinist (Jabriyya) position. The author first identifies the source of their error: a misinterpretation of the Quranic verse "Khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun" (Allah created you and what you do), which led them to believe that human actions are directly created by Allah without any human power. The author then explains the term 'safsata' (sophistry), providing its etymology from Greek through Syriac, and notes that it refers to false wisdom or fallacious argumentation. By labeling the Jabriyya doctrine as sophistry, the author indicates that it is so obviously false that no detailed refutation is needed; it contradicts basic human intuition (badahah). Every rational person instinctively knows that they have a degree of power and choice in their actions, such as eating and drinking. These actions are not forced like the blowing of wind or the rolling of a stone; they proceed from consciousness, intention, and free choice. Denying this is intellectual stubbornness (mukabarah) against the self-evident. If humans had no effective power, then the entire structure of Islamic law (taklif) would collapse, because it is unreasonable to command or prohibit someone who has no ability to act. Moreover, attributing all actions, including sins, directly to Allah would imply injustice on His part—which is impossible. The passage concludes with the Quranic verse of exaltation. This is a clear statement of the Hanafi position that affirms human acquisition (kasb) and a kind of effective power created by Allah, rejecting both Jabriyya and Qadariyya extremes.

Key Terms
سفسطة (safsata): Sophistry; a fallacious argument that appears plausible but is fundamentally false and contrary to self-evident truth.
بداهة (badahah): Self-evident knowledge that requires no proof; intuitive certainty.
جبر (jabr): Determinism; the belief that humans have no free will and all actions are directly compelled by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the Jabriyya view 'safsata'?
A) Because it contradicts the Quranic verse 'Khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun'.
B) Because it is based on Greek philosophy and false wisdom.
C) Because it denies the self-evident human experience of having power and choice in actions, which leads to the negation of moral responsibility.
D) Because it is a weak analogy (qiyas khafi).

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya view is sophistry because it contradicts self-evident human experience and would nullify the basis of religious obligation.

Defining Khala and Kasb as Relational Attributes
Providing Sadr al-Shariah's definitions of khala and kasb as relational attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khala and kasb as relational attributes and state the key difference in their loci (mahall).

Core Idea
Khala occurs outside the locus of power and is independent; kasb occurs inside the locus and is dependent.

This lesson unpacks the foundational definitions of khala and kasb as given by Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tawdih. Understanding these relational attributes is essential for grasping the Hanafi-Maturidi position on human action and the role of divine power.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate Sadr al-Shariah's definition of khala and kasb as relational attributes (amr idafi). Note that each involves a potentiality (al-muqdar) and a locus (locus of power).
2
Contrast the loci
Observe that khala places the potentiality in a non-locus of power (la mahall al-qudra), while kasb places it in the locus of power (mahall al-qudra). This spatial difference is crucial.
3
Assess independence
Notice that with khala, the agent (Allah) can be unique in bringing the potentiality into existence (yanfarid bi-ijaad). With kasb, the agent (the servant) cannot be unique; the act depends on Allah's creation.
This captures the asymmetry: God acts alone, man acts only with God's concurrent creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کہ قدرت فعل اور نفس فعل دونوں کا خالق اللہ تعالیٰ ہے اور اس قدرت مخلوقہ کے صرف واختیار کا مؤثر بندہ ہے چنانچہ بندہ جب جب اس قدرت مخلوقہ کا استعمال کرتا ہے تو اللہ عز شانہ اس فعل کا خلق فرمادیتا ہے گو کہ بعض اعیان واوقات میں جیسے منجزات انبیاء یا کرامات اولیاء کی وجہ سے صرف قدرت کے باوجود فعل کا خلق نہیں ہوتا مگر جب کوئی مانع حسی نہ ہو تو اس عزم کے وقت ضرور فعل کا وجود ہو جاتا ہے۔
اس مقام پر ماتن نے حاشیہ آرائی کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے ۔
"الفرق بين الخلق والكسب على ماقال صدر الشريعة بان الاول امر اضافي يجب ان يقع به المقدور في لامحل القدرة ويصح انفراد القادر بايجاد ذالك المقدور والثانی امراضافي يقع به المقدور فى محل القدرة ولا يصح انفراد القادر بالايجاد فالكسب لا يوجب وجود المقدور لا يعود الى محصل ينتفع به في هذا المقام كمالاً لا يخفى على دقيق المتأمل"
یعنی صدر الشریعہ نے توضیح میں خلاق و کسب کے درمیان جو فرق بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ خلق ایک امراضافی ہے جس سے مقدور قدرت کے غیر محل میں واقع ہوتا ہے یعنی اللہ کا فعل مخلوق ایسا مقدور ہے جو خالق کی قدرت کے محل میں نہیں واقع ہوتا اور اس مقدور کے ایجاد سے قادر کا منفرد ہونا صحیح ہے چنانچہ اللہ عز شانہ مستقل بلا کسب عبد مقدور کو پیدا کر سکتا ہے۔ اور کسب ایک امراضافی ہے جس سے مقصد در محل قدرت میں واقع ہوتا ہے لیکن قادر کا اس مقدور کے ایجاد سے الگ ہونا صحیح نہیں ہے چنانچہ عبد کا سب مستقل بغیر تا ثیر قدرت الہیہ مکسوب کو وجود نہیں دے سکتا غرض ، کسب مقدور کے وجود کو لازم نہیں کرتا ، اس طرح خلق و کسب کے درمیان فرق کرنا کسی ایسے ماحصل کی طرف راجع نہیں ہوتا جو اس مقام میں نفع بخش ہو جیسا کہ دوراندیش اور گہری سوچ رکھنے والے پر پوشیدہ نہیں ہے۔ فرق خلق و کسب توضیح کی درج بالا عبارت میں خلق و کسب کے درمیان دوطریقے سے فرق بیان کیا گیا ہے (۱) خلق : الہ تعالی کی ایک ایسی صفت ہے جس سے مقدور مخلوق خلاق کی قدرت کے غیر حل میں واقع ہوتا ہے۔ کسب : بندہ کی ایک ایسی صفت ہے جس سے مقدور و کسب کا سب کی قدرت کے محل میں واقع ہوتا ہے۔
اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۳۳
(۲) خلق : اللہ تعالیٰ کی ایک ایسی صفت کہ اللہ بلا احتیاج کسب کا سب علی الاستقلال پیدا کر سکتا ہے۔ کسب : ایک ایسی صفت ہے کہ بندہ کا سب بالاستقلال بلا تا ثیر قدرت الہیہ مکسوب کو وجود نہیں دے سکتا۔ مذکورہ دونوں فرقوں کے علاوہ اور طرح سے بھی علماء نے فرق کیا ہے۔
(۳) خلق ۔ وہ صفت ہے جس سے مخلوق بغیر آلہ معرض وجود میں آ جائے۔ کسب : ۔ وہ صفت ہے جو بغیر الہ وقوع پذیر نہ ہو سکے۔
(۴) خلق : قدرت قدیمہ کے تعلق کے اثر کا نام ہے۔
کسب قدرت حادثہ کے تعلق کے اثر کا نام ہے۔
جیسے حرکت زید، جو اللہ تعالیٰ کے خلق سے ذات زید میں پیدا ہوئی چنانچہ یہ حرکت اس قدرت کے محل کے غیر میں ہوئی ہے کہ قدرت کا محل اللہ تعالیٰ ہے مگر حرکت ذات زید میں ہوئی ہے اور زید کے کسب کی وجہ سے حرکت زید ہی میں پیدا ہوئی جو محل کسب ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ خالق کا اثر اس فعل کا ایجاد ہے جو اسکی ذات سے خارج ہے اور کا سب کا اثر اس فعل کی صفت میں ہوتا ہے جو کا سب کے ساتھ قائم ہے۔ قوله في الحاشية لا يعود الى محصل - يعنى صدر الشریعہ نے خلق و کسب کے درمیان جو فرق بیان کیا ہے اہل نظر کے نزدیک نفع بخش نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس پر سوال یہ ہوگا کہ کب سے کسی شئی کا وجود ہوا یا نہیں ، اگرشی کا وجود ہوا تو وہ خلق و ایجاد ہے اس تقدیر پر خلق باری تعالیٰ کے ساتھ مختص نہ رہے گا کہ بندہ کا سب کا خالق ہونا لازم آتا ہے اور اگر کسب سے کسی چیز کا وجود نہیں ہوا تو یہ کسب جبر محض کی طرف عود کر جائے گا۔ اس جگہ بعض شراح نے کہا ہے کہ ماتن نے اپنے قول لا يعود الى محصل ” سے اس دو وجہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے جس کو علامہ تفتازانی نے تلویح میں کہا ہے۔ وجہ اول : کوئی معترض کہہ سکتا ہے کہ موجودات کے واسطہ سے فعل کا وجوب مقدور عبد اور مخلوق رب ہونے کے منافی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا ممکن ہے کہ اس فعل کا استناد بندہ کی قدرت کے واسطہ سے اور اس ارادہ کے واسطہ سے ہو جسکی شان سے ترجیح و ایجاد ہے۔
That the Creator of both the power of the act and the act itself is Allah Most High, and the effective agent in the disposal and choice of this created power is the servant. Thus, whenever the servant uses this created power, Allah Most High creates the act, although in some specific instances and times—such as the miracles of prophets or the wonders of saints—the act is not created despite the existence of power; however, when there is no sensory obstacle, at the time of determination the act certainly comes into existence.
At this point, the matn author has made an annotation saying:
"The difference between creation (khala) and acquisition (kasb) according to what Sadr al-Shariah said: that the first is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in a non-locus of power, and it is valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing that potentiality into existence. The second is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in the locus of power, and it is not valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing it into existence, for acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potentiality; it does not return to a useful result in this context, as is not hidden from the sharp-minded contemplator."
Meaning: Sadr al-Shariah, in al-Tawdih, while explaining the difference between creation and acquisition, said: Creation is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in a non-locus of power—i.e., Allah's act of creation is a potentiality that does not occur in the locus of the Creator's power—and it is valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing this potentiality into existence. Thus Allah Most High can independently produce the servant's potentiality without acquisition. Acquisition is a relational attribute by which the intended occurs in the locus of power, but it is not valid for the Powerful One to be separate in bringing it into existence. Thus the servant's acquisition cannot independently give existence to the acquired without the effect of divine power. In short, acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potentiality. In this way, making a distinction between creation and acquisition does not return to a useful result that benefits in this context, as is not hidden from the far-sighted and deep thinker.
The distinction between creation and acquisition in the above expression of al-Tawdih is made in two ways: (1) Creation: an attribute of Allah Most High by which the created potentiality occurs in a non-locus of the Creator's power. Acquisition: an attribute of the servant by which the acquired potentiality occurs in the locus of the servant's power.
(2) Creation: an attribute of Allah Most High that He can independently produce the servant's acquisition without need. Acquisition: an attribute that the servant's acquisition independently cannot give existence to the acquired without the effect of divine power. Besides these two distinctions, scholars have also made distinctions in other ways.
(3) Creation: the attribute by which the created comes into existence without a tool. Acquisition: the attribute that cannot occur without a tool.
(4) Creation: the name of the effect of the attachment of the eternal power. Acquisition: the name of the effect of the attachment of the originated power.
For example, the movement of Zayd, which came into being in Zayd's essence by Allah Most High's creation. So this movement occurred outside the locus of that power, because the locus of power is Allah Most High, but the movement occurred in Zayd's essence, and due to Zayd's acquisition, it came into being in Zayd himself, which is the locus of acquisition.
The conclusion is that the effect of the Creator is the bringing into existence of the act, which is external to His essence, and the effect of the acquisition is in the attribute of the act, which subsists with the acquirer.
His statement in the annotation: "does not return to a useful result" means that the distinction Sadr al-Shariah made between creation and acquisition is not beneficial in the eyes of the people of insight, because a question would arise: does something come into existence or not? If something comes into existence, that is creation and invention; on this assumption, creation would not be exclusive to Allah Most High, as it would necessitate that the servant's acquisition is creating. And if nothing comes into existence from acquisition, then this acquisition would revert to pure coercion.
At this point, some commentators have said that the matn author, with his statement "does not return to a useful result," pointed to the two objections that Allamah Taftazani mentioned in al-Talwih. The first reason: an objector could say that the necessity of the act through means does not contradict the act being the servant's potentiality and the Lord's creation, because it is possible that the act's attribution is through the intermediary of the servant's power and through the intermediary of that will whose property is preference and creation.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis and critical refinement of the theological distinction between khala (creation) and kasb (acquisition) as discussed in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and kalam. The author begins by stating the orthodox Hanafi-Maturidi position: both the power of action and the act itself are created by Allah, but the servant has effective disposal over that created power. When the servant uses his power, Allah creates the act. Exceptions occur in miracles (mu'jizat, karamat) where the act is not created despite power, but normally the act comes into existence at the moment of determination. The matn author then quotes Sadr al-Shariah from al-Tawdih, who defines khala as a relational attribute (amr idafi) where the potentiality occurs outside the locus of power, and the agent can act alone. Kasb is where the potentiality occurs within the locus of power (the servant), and the agent cannot act alone. The commentary then elaborates four distinctions: (1) khala occurs outside the locus of God's power, kasb occurs in the servant's locus; (2) khala is independent, kasb is dependent on divine power; (3) khala occurs without an instrument, kasb requires an instrument; (4) khala is the effect of eternal power, kasb is the effect of originated power. An example of Zayd's movement illustrates that the movement is God's creation in Zayd, but it is also Zayd's kasb because it occurs in him. The author then discusses the critique from Taftazani's al-Talwih: Sadr al-Shariah's distinction is not beneficial because it leads to a dilemma—if acquisition produces existence, then the servant creates (undermining God's exclusive creation); if it produces none, then kasb reduces to mere compulsion. Taftazani responds that the necessity of the act through means (intermediary of power and will) does not negate that the act is the servant's potentiality and God's creation, because the attribution is through the servant's power and will, which are themselves created means.

Key Terms
خلق (khala): A relational attribute of Allah by which the potentiality occurs in a non-locus of power, and He can bring it into existence independently.
كسب (kasb): A relational attribute of the servant by which the potentiality occurs in the locus of his power, but he cannot bring it into existence independently; it requires Allah's creation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sadr al-Shariah's definition, what is the key difference between khala and kasb?
A) Khala occurs in the locus of power, kasb occurs outside it.
B) Khala is a relational attribute where the potentiality occurs outside the locus of power and the agent can be unique in bringing it about; kasb occurs in the locus of power and the agent cannot be unique.
C) Khala requires an instrument, kasb does not.
D) Khala is the effect of originated power, kasb is the effect of eternal power.

Key Takeaway
Khala and kasb are two distinct relational attributes: one divine (independent creation outside the power locus), one human (dependent acquisition inside the power locus).

intermediate
10 min
Four Distinctions Between Khala and Kasb
Enumerating four scholarly distinctions between khala and kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the four distinctions between khala and kasb enumerated in the text.

Core Idea
Khala is independent, eternal, instrument-free; kasb is dependent, temporal, and requires means.

Beyond Sadr al-Shariah's foundational definition, scholars have elaborated four concrete distinctions between khala and kasb. These distinctions highlight the ontological and operational differences between the divine and human roles in action.

Guided Path
1
Review the first two distinctions
These are based on locus (outside vs. inside) and independence (unique creation vs. dependent acquisition). They are directly from Sadr al-Shariah.
2
Learn the third distinction: instrument
Khala brings about existence without any tool (āla); kasb cannot occur without a tool. This reflects that human actions require bodily means, while divine creation is immediate.
3
Learn the fourth distinction: power type
Khala is the effect of eternal power (qudra qadīma); kasb is the effect of originated power (qudra ḥāditha). This links to the theological attribute of God's timeless power vs. man's contingent power.
4
Apply to the example of Zayd's movement
Use the given example to see each distinction in operation: the movement's existence is khala (no instrument for God, by eternal power); its acquisition by Zayd is kasb (through Zayd's body and his originated power).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کہ قدرت فعل اور نفس فعل دونوں کا خالق اللہ تعالیٰ ہے اور اس قدرت مخلوقہ کے صرف واختیار کا مؤثر بندہ ہے چنانچہ بندہ جب جب اس قدرت مخلوقہ کا استعمال کرتا ہے تو اللہ عز شانہ اس فعل کا خلق فرمادیتا ہے گو کہ بعض اعیان واوقات میں جیسے منجزات انبیاء یا کرامات اولیاء کی وجہ سے صرف قدرت کے باوجود فعل کا خلق نہیں ہوتا مگر جب کوئی مانع حسی نہ ہو تو اس عزم کے وقت ضرور فعل کا وجود ہو جاتا ہے۔
اس مقام پر ماتن نے حاشیہ آرائی کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے ۔
"الفرق بين الخلق والكسب على ماقال صدر الشريعة بان الاول امر اضافي يجب ان يقع به المقدور في لامحل القدرة ويصح انفراد القادر بايجاد ذالك المقدور والثانی امراضافي يقع به المقدور فى محل القدرة ولا يصح انفراد القادر بالايجاد فالكسب لا يوجب وجود المقدور لا يعود الى محصل ينتفع به في هذا المقام كمالاً لا يخفى على دقيق المتأمل"

That the Creator of both the power of the act and the act itself is Allah Most High, and the effective agent in the disposal and choice of this created power is the servant. Commentary
