The matn author then quotes Sadr al-Shariah from al-Tawdih, who defines khala as a relational attribute (amr idafi) where the potentiality occurs outside the locus of power, and the agent can act alone. Kasb is where the potentiality occurs within the locus of power (the servant), and the agent cannot act alone. The commentary then elaborates four distinctions: (1) khala occurs outside the locus of God's power, kasb occurs in the servant's locus; (2) khala is independent, kasb is dependent on divine power; (3) khala occurs without an instrument, kasb requires an instrument; (4) khala is the effect of eternal power, kasb is the effect of originated power. An example of Zayd's movement illustrates that the movement is God's creation in Zayd, but it is also Zayd's kasb because it occurs in him. The author then discusses the critique from Taftazani's al-Talwih: Sadr al-Shariah's distinction is not beneficial because it leads to a dilemma—if acquisition produces existence, then the servant creates (undermining God's exclusive creation); if it produces none, then kasb reduces to mere compulsion. Taftazani responds that the necessity of the act through means (intermediary of power and will) does not negate that the act is the servant's potentiality and God's creation, because the attribution is through the servant's power and will, which are themselves created means.

Key Terms
قدرة قديمة (qudra qadīma): The eternal power of Allah, which is a necessary attribute; its effect is creation (khala).
قدرة حادثة (qudra ḥāditha): The originated (created) power in the servant, contingent and dependent; its effect is acquisition (kasb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four distinctions between khala and kasb mentioned in the passage?
A) Locus of occurrence (outside vs. inside power locus)
B) Independence of the agent (can be unique vs. cannot be unique)
C) Use of an instrument (without vs. with tool)
D) Temporal priority (khala happens first, kasb later)

Key Takeaway
The four distinctions—locus, independence, instrumentality, and power type—provide a comprehensive framework for understanding the simultaneous divine creation and human acquisition of actions.

The Critique of Sadr al-Shariah's Distinction and the Response
Critiquing and defending Sadr al-Shariah's distinction between khala and kasb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the critique of Sadr al-Shariah's distinction and the Hanafi response that resolves the dilemma.

Core Idea
The critique exposes a dilemma: either kasb creates existence (undermining divine exclusivity) or it is nothing (reducing to compulsion); the response navigates via attribution through means.

Sadr al-Shariah's distinction, while clear, is criticized as not fully benefical because it leads to a theological dilemma. The commentator cites Taftazani's response, which argues that the act's necessity through created means does not negate the act's attribution to both God and the servant. This lesson explores that critique and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the critique
Find the two horns of the dilemma: if kasb produces existence, then the servant creates (contradicting divine exclusivity); if it produces none, then kasb is mere compulsion (Jabriyya).
2
Understand why the distinction is called 'not beneficial'
The author says the distinction 'does not return to a useful result' (lā yaʿūdu ilā muḥaṣṣal). This is because it leaves the dilemma unresolved.
3
Learn the response from Taftazani
The response asserts that the necessity of an act through means (intermediary of power and will) does not contradict the act being both servant's potentiality and Lord's creation. The act is attributed to the servant through his power and will, but those means are themselves created.
4
Apply the resolution to the example
In Zayd's movement, the means (Zayd's power and will) necessitate the movement, but this necessity does not make Zayd the creator; rather, it is a conditioned necessity within God's creation. Thus, kasb is real but not creative.

جیسے حرکت زید، جو اللہ تعالیٰ کے خلق سے ذات زید میں پیدا ہوئی چنانچہ یہ حرکت اس قدرت کے محل کے غیر میں ہوئی ہے کہ قدرت کا محل اللہ تعالیٰ ہے مگر حرکت ذات زید میں ہوئی ہے اور زید کے کسب کی وجہ سے حرکت زید ہی میں پیدا ہوئی جو محل کسب ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ خالق کا اثر اس فعل کا ایجاد ہے جو اسکی ذات سے خارج ہے اور کا سب کا اثر اس فعل کی صفت میں ہوتا ہے جو کا سب کے ساتھ قائم ہے۔ قوله في الحاشية لا يعود الى محصل - يعنى صدر الشریعہ نے خلق و کسب کے درمیان جو فرق بیان کیا ہے اہل نظر کے نزدیک نفع بخش نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس پر سوال یہ ہوگا کہ کب سے کسی شئی کا وجود ہوا یا نہیں ، اگرشی کا وجود ہوا تو وہ خلق و ایجاد ہے اس تقدیر پر خلق باری تعالیٰ کے ساتھ مختص نہ رہے گا کہ بندہ کا سب کا خالق ہونا لازم آتا ہے اور اگر کسب سے کسی چیز کا وجود نہیں ہوا تو یہ کسب جبر محض کی طرف عود کر جائے گا۔ اس جگہ بعض شراح نے کہا ہے کہ ماتن نے اپنے قول لا يعود الى محصل ” سے اس دو وجہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے جس کو علامہ تفتازانی نے تلویح میں کہا ہے۔ وجہ اول : کوئی معترض کہہ سکتا ہے کہ موجودات کے واسطہ سے فعل کا وجوب مقدور عبد اور مخلوق رب ہونے کے منافی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا ممکن ہے کہ اس فعل کا استناد بندہ کی قدرت کے واسطہ سے اور اس ارادہ کے واسطہ سے ہو جسکی شان سے ترجیح و ایجاد ہے۔
That the Creator of both the power of the act and the act itself is Allah Most High, and the effective agent in the disposal and choice of this created power is the servant. Thus, whenever the servant uses this created power, Allah Most High creates the act, although in some specific instances and times—such as the miracles of prophets or the wonders of saints—the act is not created despite the existence of power; however, when there is no sensory obstacle, at the time of determination the act certainly comes into existence.
At this point, the matn author has made an annotation saying:
"The difference between creation (khala) and acquisition (kasb) according to what Sadr al-Shariah said: that the first is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in a non-locus of power, and it is valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing that potentiality into existence. The second is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in the locus of power, and it is not valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing it into existence, for acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potentiality; it does not return to a useful result in this context, as is not hidden from the sharp-minded contemplator."
Meaning: Sadr al-Shariah, in al-Tawdih, while explaining the difference between creation and acquisition, said: Creation is a relational attribute by which the potentiality occurs in a non-locus of power—i.e., Allah's act of creation is a potentiality that does not occur in the locus of the Creator's power—and it is valid for the Powerful One to be unique in bringing this potentiality into existence. Thus Allah Most High can independently produce the servant's potentiality without acquisition. Acquisition is a relational attribute by which the intended occurs in the locus of power, but it is not valid for the Powerful One to be separate in bringing it into existence. Thus the servant's acquisition cannot independently give existence to the acquired without the effect of divine power. In short, acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potentiality. In this way, making a distinction between creation and acquisition does not return to a useful result that benefits in this context, as is not hidden from the far-sighted and deep thinker.
The distinction between creation and acquisition in the above expression of al-Tawdih is made in two ways: (1) Creation: an attribute of Allah Most High by which the created potentiality occurs in a non-locus of the Creator's power. Acquisition: an attribute of the servant by which the acquired potentiality occurs in the locus of the servant's power.
(2) Creation: an attribute of Allah Most High that He can independently produce the servant's acquisition without need. Acquisition: an attribute that the servant's acquisition independently cannot give existence to the acquired without the effect of divine power. Besides these two distinctions, scholars have also made distinctions in other ways.
(3) Creation: the attribute by which the created comes into existence without a tool. Acquisition: the attribute that cannot occur without a tool.
(4) Creation: the name of the effect of the attachment of the eternal power. Acquisition: the name of the effect of the attachment of the originated power.
For example, the movement of Zayd, which came into being in Zayd's essence by Allah Most High's creation. So this movement occurred outside the locus of that power, because the locus of power is Allah Most High, but the movement occurred in Zayd's essence, and due to Zayd's acquisition, it came into being in Zayd himself, which is the locus of acquisition.
The conclusion is that the effect of the Creator is the bringing into existence of the act, which is external to His essence, and the effect of the acquisition is in the attribute of the act, which subsists with the acquirer.
His statement in the annotation: "does not return to a useful result" means that the distinction Sadr al-Shariah made between creation and acquisition is not beneficial in the eyes of the people of insight, because a question would arise: does something come into existence or not? If something comes into existence, that is creation and invention; on this assumption, creation would not be exclusive to Allah Most High, as it would necessitate that the servant's acquisition is creating. And if nothing comes into existence from acquisition, then this acquisition would revert to pure coercion.
At this point, some commentators have said that the matn author, with his statement "does not return to a useful result," pointed to the two objections that Allamah Taftazani mentioned in al-Talwih. The first reason: an objector could say that the necessity of the act through means does not contradict the act being the servant's potentiality and the Lord's creation, because it is possible that the act's attribution is through the intermediary of the servant's power and through the intermediary of that will whose property is preference and creation.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis and critical refinement of the theological distinction between khala (creation) and kasb (acquisition) as discussed in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and kalam. The author begins by stating the orthodox Hanafi-Maturidi position: both the power of action and the act itself are created by Allah, but the servant has effective disposal over that created power. When the servant uses his power, Allah creates the act. Exceptions occur in miracles (mu'jizat, karamat) where the act is not created despite power, but normally the act comes into existence at the moment of determination. The matn author then quotes Sadr al-Shariah from al-Tawdih, who defines khala as a relational attribute (amr idafi) where the potentiality occurs outside the locus of power, and the agent can act alone. Kasb is where the potentiality occurs within the locus of power (the servant), and the agent cannot act alone. The commentary then elaborates four distinctions: (1) khala occurs outside the locus of God's power, kasb occurs in the servant's locus; (2) khala is independent, kasb is dependent on divine power; (3) khala occurs without an instrument, kasb requires an instrument; (4) khala is the effect of eternal power, kasb is the effect of originated power. An example of Zayd's movement illustrates that the movement is God's creation in Zayd, but it is also Zayd's kasb because it occurs in him. The author then discusses the critique from Taftazani's al-Talwih: Sadr al-Shariah's distinction is not beneficial because it leads to a dilemma—if acquisition produces existence, then the servant creates (undermining God's exclusive creation); if it produces none, then kasb reduces to mere compulsion. Taftazani responds that the necessity of the act through means (intermediary of power and will) does not negate that the act is the servant's potentiality and God's creation, because the attribution is through the servant's power and will, which are themselves created means.

Key Terms
وسائط (wasāʾiṭ): Means or intermediaries; in this context, the servant's power and will are created means through which the act is necessitated from Allah.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion; the view that humans have no real choice or efficacy in actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does Taftazani's response resolve the dilemma of Sadr al-Shariah's distinction?
A) By denying that kasb exists at all.
B) By arguing that the servant's power and will are created means that necessitate the act from Allah, thus kasb is real without being creative.
C) By asserting that the servant creates his own power, so he is partially responsible.
D) By claiming that both creation and acquisition are purely metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The critique of Sadr al-Shariah's distinction is resolved by Taftazani's insight that human power and will are created means that necessitate the act from Allah—preserving both divine exclusivity in creation and human reality in acquisition.

Defining Husn li-Ghayrihi and Its First Division
Defining husn li-ghayrihi and its first division with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define husn li-ghayrihi and identify its first division using examples from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Husn li-ghayrihi: an act's goodness comes from an external, non-voluntary intermediary.

This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut introduces the concept of husn li-ghayrihi, where an act lacks intrinsic goodness but acquires it through an external factor. The author explains its first division, where the servant has no choice over the intermediary, and illustrates with zakat, fasting, and hajj. Understanding this classification is fundamental to Hanafi usul al-fiqh for determining the legal value of actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its definition
Find the term 'husn li-ghayrihi' in the passage and state its definition: an act that has no intrinsic goodness, but receives goodness from an external intermediary.
The intermediary can be essential (wasita fi al-thubut) or incidental (wasita fi al-urud).
2
Distinguish intrinsic vs. derived goodness
Compare husn li-aynihi (intrinsic goodness) with husn li-ghayrihi. In the latter, the intellect initially sees the act as good but later realizes the goodness is from another source.
This distinction affects how acts are categorized in fiqh.
3
Analyze the first division's condition
The first division of husn li-ghayrihi requires that the servant has no choice over the intermediary. The act becomes good due to a factor beyond the servant's control.
Examples: need of the poor, the soul, the House (Kaaba)—all are non-voluntary from the servant's side.
4
Apply the definition to examples
Examine the examples: zakat, fasting, hajj. For each, identify the external intermediary (need of poor, subduing soul, honor of House) and confirm that the servant has no choice over that intermediary.
The passage provides two interpretations of the matn, but both emphasize the non-voluntary nature of the intermediary.

توجیہ یہ ہے کہ فعل زکوۃ، صوم اور حج کے لئے واسطہ، دفع حاجت فقیر، ہر نفس، اور شرف بیت ہے. دوسری توجیہ یہ ہے کہ واسطہ صرف حاجت نفس اور بیت ہیں۔ پہلی توجیہ کے مطابق زکوۃ مشروع ہوئی ہے حاجت فقیر کو دفع کرنے کیلئے ، صوم مشروع ہوا ہے قبر نفس کے لئے اور حج مشروع ہوا ہے شرف بیت کے لئے مگر یہ واضح امر ہے کہ دفع حاجت فقیر کے لئے ، حاجت ضروری ہے، قہر نفس کے لئے نفس لازم ہے اور شرف بیت کے لئے بیت اللہ ضروری ہے اس لئے ان امور و افعال کے مشروعیت کی نسبت دفع حاجت ، قہر نفس، اور شرف بیت کی طرف نہ کر کے زکوۃ کی مشروعیت کی نسبت صرف حاجت کی طرف کی گئی ہے، مشروعیت صوم کی نسبت قہر نفس کیطرف نہ کر کے صرف نفس کی طرف کی گئی اسی طرح مشروعیت حج کی نسبت شرف بیت کی طرف نہ کر کے محض بیت کی طرف کی گئی غرضیکہ اس تقدیر پر زکوۃ، صوم، حج کیلئے وسائط دفع حاجت اور شرف بیت ہیں مگر مشروعیت کی نسبت مضاف کے بجائے مضاف الیہ کی طرف مناسبت کیوجہ سے کی گئی ہے۔ اور یہ وہ وسائط ہیں جسمیں بندہ کو اختیار حاصل نہیں ہے چنانچہ شرف بیت میں بندہ کا غیر مختار ہونا ظاہر ہے اور دفع حاجت فقیر میں نظر کرتے ہوئے حاجت کی طرف بندہ غیر مختار ہے کیونکہ حاجت فقیر اختیاری نہیں ہے بلکہ محض اللہ عز شانہ کے پیدا کرنے سے ہے۔ رہا قہر نفس کا غیر اختیاری ہونا تو یہ بھی نظر کرتے ہوئے
His statement: 'And that which belongs to other than it is appended to the first, and it is concerning what...' The author mentioned the second type of actions, namely husn li-ghayrihi and its divisions. Husn li-ghayrihi is called that which has no intrinsic goodness nor does it enter into goodness, rather goodness comes to it due to another, that other either being an intermediary in subsistence or an intermediary in occurrence. Husn li-ghayrihi also has two divisions: (1) husn li-ghayr al-haqq bi'l-husn li-'aynihi: meaning the act in itself has no goodness, but due to being joined to another, goodness comes to the act. This division occurs in an act in which the servant has no choice. So this other will not be a voluntary act at that time; rather, that other is merely an intermediary and ambassador to establish goodness in the act. It is called 'appended to the first' or 'appended to intrinsic goodness' because although this other is an intermediary for the establishment of goodness in the act, when the intellect observes this attribute in the act, at first glance it judges that this attribute is due to the essence of the act. However, when the intellect then perceives its cause, it becomes known that this attribute is established in the act in consideration of the other. For this reason, it is called 'appended to intrinsic goodness.' Like zakat, fasting, hajj: in consideration of the need of the poor, the soul, and the House, they are legislated. His statement: 'like zakat and fasting' – note that the author's phrase 'like zakat, fasting, and hajj' can be explained in two ways. The first explanation is that for the acts of zakat, fasting, and hajj, the intermediaries are repelling the need of the poor, subduing the soul, and the honor of the House. The second explanation is that the intermediaries are only the need, the soul, and the House. According to the first explanation, zakat is legislated to repel the need of the poor, fasting is legislated for the subduing of the soul, and hajj is legislated for the honor of the House. But it is clear that repelling the need of the poor requires need, subduing the soul requires the soul, and honoring the House requires the House of Allah. So the legislation of these acts is not attributed to repelling need, etc., but rather the legislation of zakat is attributed only to need, the legislation of fasting is attributed only to the soul, and the legislation of hajj is attributed only to the House. In short, on this basis, for zakat, fasting, and hajj, the intermediaries are repelling need and the honor of the House, but the attribution of legislation is made to the object of the construct (mudaf ilayh) due to suitability. And these are intermediaries in which the servant has no choice. So in the honor of the House, the servant's lack of choice is apparent, and in repelling the need of the poor, in consideration of the need, the servant has no choice because the need of the poor is not voluntary but purely from Allah. As for the subduing of the soul being non-voluntary, this is also in consideration...
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage defines husn li-ghayrihi (goodness derived from another). The author explains that an act has no intrinsic goodness but receives goodness from an external intermediary. There are two divisions of husn li-ghayrihi; only the first division is detailed here: where the servant has no choice, and the intermediary is such that at first glance the goodness seems intrinsic but is actually derived from another. Examples are zakat, fasting, and hajj, whose legislation is based on external factors like need of the poor, soul, and the House (Kaaba). The author provides two interpretations of the matn's phrasing, emphasizing that the intermediaries are non-voluntary from the servant's side.

Key Terms
حسن لغیرہ (husn li-ghayrihi): Goodness derived from an external intermediary, not intrinsic to the act.
واسطہ فی الثبوت (wasita fi al-thubut): An intermediary that is essential for the existence of the act's goodness.
واسطہ فی العروض (wasita fi al-urud): An intermediary that is incidental, causing goodness to appear in the act.
ملحق بالحسن لعینہ (mulhaq bi al-husn li-'aynihi): Appended to intrinsic goodness; a case where goodness seems intrinsic but is actually derived from another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an example of husn li-ghayrihi according to the first division?
A) Daily prayers
B) Zakat
C) Offering sacrifices
D) Jihad

Key Takeaway
Husn li-ghayrihi describes acts whose goodness is derived from an external, non-voluntary intermediary, like zakat from the need of the poor.
